In order to be considered “non-resident” in the respective definitive rankings students who are successful in the rankings of 7 November 2025 (only if the contract was registered after 31 October 2025) and those included in the rankings of 16 December 2025 (only if the contract was registered after 15 November 2025) may also self-certify paid accommodation in this time frame to obtain a supplement of the grant amount from “commuter” to “non-resident”, if funds are available.</td></tr></table>

Students enrolled in a bachelor's, single-cycle master’s degree, or master’s degree course are required to take paid accommodation for 10 months, included in the period from 1 September 2025 to 30 September 2026 (or 5 months if students are applying for an additional semester, included in the period from 1 September 2025 to 31 March 2026) and to complete the appropriate self-certification online, in accordance with the procedures and time frames set out in this paragraph. 

Students enrolled in a PhD/specialisation school are required to have paid accommodation for 10 months, included in the period from 1 October 2025 to 31 March 2027, and to complete an online self-certification, in accordance with the procedures and time frames set out in this paragraph. 

Art. 8(2.1) SPECIFIC PROVISIONS FOR STUDENTS OF COURSES WITH A "FILTER SEMESTER". (CLASSES LM-41, LM-46, LM-42) 

Students attending the “filter semester” for one of the courses belonging to the LM-41, LM-42 or LM-46 classes (medicina e chirurgia, medicina veterinaria e Odontoiatria e protesi dentaria courses) must self-certify accommodation for the period 

# between 5 and 13 March 2026 at 12 noon

in order to be considered “non-resident” in the final rankings of 26 March 2026. 

Students who do NOT attend the "filter semester" in Piedmont, but who continue their studies by enrolling in the second semester at a Piedmont university as non-resident students, pursuant to art. 4 of this notice, and students who attend the "filter semester" in Piedmont, but who continue their studies by enrolling in a different Piedmont university, moving from resident/commuter to nonresident students, must have and declare at least three months of paid accommodation in the academic year 2025/26 to be considered non-resident. 

For such students, the amount of the “non-resident” scholarship will be calculated in proportion to the number of months covered by a paid lease agreement, provided that it is three months or more, also including any period spent during the filter semester. 48 

There are no exceptions regarding the minimum duration of paid accommodation (10 months in the academic year 2025/26) for students who attend the "filter semester" in Piedmont as non-resident students and continue their studies by enrolling in the second semester at the same university in Piedmont. to compete for the amount provided for "non-resident" students pursuant to art. 5(1.3) of this notice. 

The procedures for submitting the paid accommodation declaration are the same as those set out in art. 8(2) of this notice. 

For these students too, it will be possible to declare any supplement to the contract between 20 March and 10 April 2026 (by noon), following the same procedures as described in art. 8(2). 

SECTION III SPECIFIC PROVISIONS FOR FIRST YEARS 

# ART. 9 WHO CAN APPLY: ADMISSION REQUIREMENTS

This section is aimed at students enrolling in the academic year 2025/26, in a first year of a bachelor's degree, master's degree or single-cycle master's degree, first and second Level academic diploma (AFAM). 

Students who have transferred or are transferring from another University, including from outside Piedmont, may not apply as a first-year but must apply as a subsequent-year student (art. 15(1.3)) 

In the case of part-time enrolment, you may only submit a standard application and may NOT benefit from the Scholarship for the additional semester. 

![image](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2026-02-26/96fe0d1f-109c-4be1-a3cb-bd4e5e023921/6112dd32f10484cda4a363245c438970a0adf46ac209f60aa1cb17b0e5ae2701.jpg)


Students must submit their applications within the deadlines specified in art. 10(2) even if they were not yet duly enrolled at the time of submitting the application. Should students enrol in a course other than the one indicated in their application, they must promptly notify EDISU of the change in the manner indicated in art. 7(5) and (6). 

Students attending the “filter semester” of medicina e chirurgia, medicina veterinaria e odontoiatria e protesi dentaria courses, even at a non-Piedmont university, must follow the instructions in paragraph 3 below 

# Art. 9(1) REQUIREMENTS FOR ADMISSION TO THE COMPETITION

In addition to the financial requirements (art. 6), the following eligibility requirements are required when submitting the application and will be checked when the provisional and final scholarship rankings are drawn up. 

Merit requirements are only required for the disbursement of the second instalment and to maintain the right to the first instalment already awarded or to maintain eligibility, in accordance with the methods and time frames set out in art. 13 below, except as provided for in paragraph 2 of this article in the case of awards from previous careers.

Students may apply after withdrawing from studies regardless of when the withdrawal was made. 

If they apply for a scholarship after withdrawing from their studies or losing their student status and they have benefited from the scholarship or grant and accommodation service for one or more academic years during their previous course enrolment, by enrolling in a new course, they will be prevented from applying for benefits from EDISU for the same number of years as they benefited from these benefits during their previous enrolment. This is true even if they have withdrawn from a bachelor’s degree or master's degree course and have subsequently enrolled in a single-cycle master's degree course, and vice versa. The only exception is if they return the scholarship received by 12 November 2025, the deadline for submitting complaints. 

# Art. 9(1.1) COURSE TRANSFERS AND TRANSFERS FROM OTHER UNIVERSITIES

Students already enrolled in the Italian university system in previous academic years who change course within the same University or transfer from another University, even if not in Piedmont, may NOT submit an application as a first-year student but must apply as a subsequent-year student, regardless of the course year in which they are enrolled by the university or AFAM 

A change of course within the same University is not equivalent to a career break. Therefore, following a switch, the year of first enrolment will be considered to be that of the previous course and an application cannot be submitted as a first-year student. Such students must refer to art. 15(4) of the Subsequent-Years Section. 

In the case of both course and university transfers, only the number of credits recognised pursuant to art. 15(4) will be taken into account for the calculation of the merit requirements. 

# Art. 9(2) CREDIT RECOGNITION (SHORTENING OF CAREER, SINGLE COURSES, PREVIOUS CAREERS)

Students who obtain 

a) a career shortening50, as a result of the recognition of credits related to degrees obtained or examinations taken at a foreign University 

b) recognition of credits from individual courses/modules previously taken 

c) recognition of credits from a previous career that ended due to withdrawal or loss of status 

will be considered as enrolled in a first year or as enrolled in a year subsequent to the first in the EDISU rankings according to the number of credits recognised, as described below. 

1. Bachelor’s degrees courses 

a. 0 to 24 credits: first year. 

b. 25 to 79 credits: second year. 

c. 80 to 134 credits: third year. 

d. 135 or more credits: additional semester. 

2. Master’s degree courses 

a. 0 to 29 credits: first year. 

b. 30 to 79 credits: second year. 

c. 80 or more credits: additional semester. 

3. Single-cycle master’s degree courses 

a. 0 to 24 credits: first year. 

b. 25 to 79 credits: second year. 

c. 80 to 134 credits: third year. 

d. 135 to 189 credits: fourth year. 

e. 190 to 244 credits: fifth year. 

f. 245 to 299 credits: sixth year. 

g. 300 or more credits: additional semester. 

The above table is conditional on the possibility of achieving the required credits in the career plan. Otherwise, please refer to art. 15(2) and Annex A2. 

Credits recognised for various reasons (career shortening, single courses, previous careers) are added together for the purpose of assessing the year of enrolment, even if the recognition took place in an academic year prior to 2025/26. 

Only the total credits provided by the Universities will be considered valid; any discrepancies between the credits declared by students and those confirmed by the University must be clarified by students at their own University. 

It should be noted that for students with a disability of $6 6 \%$ or more or recognition of a disability pursuant to art. 3(1) and/or (3) of Law 104/1992, the number of validated credits is reduced pursuant to art. 29(3.2) below, while for part-time students it is reduced pursuant to art. 15(2). 

If, at the time of submitting their application, students have already applied to their University for the foreign career shortening, recognition of individual courses/modules, or validation of credits from their previous career ended due to withdrawal or loss of status, they must declare this by means of the special procedure in the “Scholastic data” section of the online application. 

If credits are recognised 

1. before submitting the application: students are required to declare this by means of the special option available under the “Scholastic data” section of the application; 

2. after submitting the application, but no later than 12 November 2025 (31 October for students enrolled in bachelor’s degree and single-cycle master’s degree courses): students are required to notify EDISU of this by filling in the relevant complaint in the special section or by opening a ticket as an accredited user. 

3. after 12 November 2025 (31 October for students enrolled in bachelor’s degree and single-cycle master’s degree courses): students are required to notify EDISU of this by filling in the relevant complaint in the special section or by opening a ticket as an accredited user but will be considered as a first-year student for the current academic year 2025/26. However, in the academic year $2 0 2 6 / 2 7 ,$ these students will be placed in the correct year according to the number of credits recognised. 

If students have not taken any examinations in Italy, the average lowest C-level grade of the ECTS average of the course attended, communicated to EDISU by the University, will be taken into account for the calculation of the merit mark. 

The above provisions also apply in the case of “early registration” from March 2025. 

Students who have applied for the foreign career shortening (point a of this subsection) are in any case required to meet the merit requirements indicated in subsections 5 (if successful) and 6 (if eligible) of article 13 below, otherwise any benefits they may have received will be revoked. Only examinations passed at one's own University in Piedmont may be counted in the credits required, not those taken abroad and recognised by the University for career shortening purposes. The payment of the second scholarship instalment is conditional on the achievement of 20 credits by 10 August 2026 for students enrolled full-time or 11 credits if enrolled part-time. 

If these credits are not obtained by 30 November 2026, the scholarship and/or the value of the accommodation service used in accordance with art. 38 will be revoked. 

![image](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2026-02-26/96fe0d1f-109c-4be1-a3cb-bd4e5e023921/f4d6c0972e1ab64b48769b97af5a00cebfcec8e832f761fe4e7a8c4c21210dd9.jpg)


# 9(3) SPECIFIC PROVISIONS FOR STUDENTS OF COURSES WITH A "FILTER SEMESTER" (CLASSES LM-41, LM-46, LM-42)

Students of courses pertaining to the 5- or 6-year postgraduate degree in medicina e chirurgia, e courses (LM-41), the 5- or 6-year postgraduate degree in Odontoiatria e protesi dentaria (LM-46) or the 5- or 6-year postgraduate degree in medicina veterinaria (LM-42) (henceforth, Classes LM-41, LM-46 and LM-42) must submit a scholarship application to the reference Agency for the Right to Education for the university where they are attending the “filter semester”. 

Please note: students attending one of the courses in Classes LM-41, LM-46 or LM-42 are advised to carefully check the specific provisions laid down by each reference Agency for the Right to Education for the location where they are attending the filter semester and where they intend to continue their studies. 

# 9(3.1) STUDENTS ATTENDING THE "FILTER SEMESTER" IN PIEDMONT

Students attending the “filter semester” for one of the courses belonging to the Classes LM-41 or LM-46 or LM-42 at a Piedmont University, must submit the scholarship or scholarship and accommodation service (if a non-resident student) application to EDISU Piemonte by 9 September 2025 at 12 noon, according to the methods indicated in art. 10 below. 

The application must be completed exclusively by indicating the details of one of the courses, from those belonging to Classes LM-41 or LM-46 or LM-42, for which you intend to attend the “filter semester”. 

Indicating a "related course" is not permitted, not even for the purpose of claiming the $20 \%$ increase for the second course. 

These students will appear with the outcome “suspended for filter semester enrolment” in the final December scholarship rankings. Please refer to art. 12 for provisions on the publication of rankings and the submission of any claims. 

# 9(3.2) STUDENTS NOT ATTENDING THE "FILTER SEMESTER" IN PIEDMONT

Students who, though not attending the filter semester at a Piedmont university, indicate it as one of the ten locations where they intend to continue their studies, in accordance with art. 2 of Ministerial Decree no. 418 of 30 May 2025, may also apply to EDISU Piemonte. In this case, the application must include the details of the course, from those belonging to Classes LM-41 or LM-46 or LM-42, offered by the Piedmont University. 

These students will appear with the outcome “suspended for filter semester enrolment” in the final December scholarship rankings. Please refer to art. 12 for provisions on the publication of rankings and the submission of any claims. 

Students who do NOT submit an application to EDISU Piemonte by 9 September 2025 will only be able to access an extraordinary application procedure. This is provided that they have submitted, by the relevant deadlines, an application for a scholarship to the competent Agency for the Right to Education for the university where they are attending the "filter semester". This procedure will be reserved for those who intend to continue their studies at a Piedmont university and will be active from 26 January to 16 February 2026 at 12 noon, in accordance with the procedures to be defined in a special notice published in the days preceding the opening of the procedure. 

EDISU Piemonte will implement any provision issued by the MUR after the publication of this notice and will communicate it to students concerned 

# ART. 10 METHODS AND DEADLINES FOR SUBMITTING AN APPLICATION

# Art. 10(1) METHOD FOR SUBMITTING THE APPLICATION

Applications can be submitted from 25 July 2025. The application submission methods are set out in art. 7(1.1) (for students with a SPID or CIE) and (1.2) (for international students without residence in Italy with a Temporary Access Code). International students with a household resident abroad must follow the application submission methods outlined in arts. 30 and 31. 

Students who are minors on the application deadline date must have their parents/guardians complete the scholarship application authorisation form, available on the EDISU website in the Documentazione $>$ Modulistica> Borse e altri contributi (Documentation $>$ Forms $>$ Grants and other contributions) section, which must be attached to the application in the upload relating to the identity document, together with the parents' identity document. 

For crediting the IBAN, they must verify what is stated in art. 7(3). 

![image](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2026-02-26/96fe0d1f-109c-4be1-a3cb-bd4e5e023921/4b9f3f57d66b61e567405a6159c7873115b986ad9e9379ab04f8591bd9657c88.jpg)


Students must submit their applications within the deadlines specified in the following table, even if they were not yet duly enrolled at the time of submitting the application. Should they enrol in a course other than the one indicated in their application, they must promptly notify EDISU of the change in the manner indicated in art. 7(5) and (6). 

Any event occurring after the date on which the application is submitted (award of another scholarship or other financial aid, transfer to another university, withdrawal from studies, change of commitment from part-time to full-time and vice versa, inability to continue studies, withdrawal from enrolment, change of department or course of study, change of course venue, etc.) must be promptly communicated to the EDISU offices and documented by opening a ticket. EDISU will check that the requirements are still met and will take any measures necessary to revoke benefits. If this is not the case, EDISU reserves the right to take action in relation to the failure to notify. In the event of transfer to another University in Piedmont, students will be placed at the bottom of the ranking of the new University and course level 

In the event of transfer to another University outside Piedmont or withdrawal from studies after the publication of the definitive rankings and during the academic year, the benefit won or the eligibility condition will be revoked. 

# Art. 10(2) DEADLINE FOR SUBMITTING THE APPLICATION

<table><tr><td>REQUEST TYPE</td><td>DEADLINE</td></tr><tr><td>SCHOLARSHIP AND ACCOMMODATION SERVICE</td><td>9 SEPTEMBER 12:00 P.M.</td></tr><tr><td>SCHOLARSHIP</td><td>9 SEPTEMBER 12:00 P.M.</td></tr></table>

The online application must always be submitted by 12:00 p.m. on the deadline day. This procedure closes automatically at 12:00 p.m. on that day and the countdown is reset. 

After 12:00 p.m. of the deadline, it will not be possible to submit the application even if the failure to submit is due to force majeure or the fault of a third party (e.g. problems with the internet connection or the terminal being used). 

For international students not resident in Italy who submit their application with a Temporary Access Code, transmission by 12:00 p.m. will only be possible after attaching the signed PDF of the application and a copy of their valid identity document. 

It can take up to 6 hours from the request for the Temporary Access Code for it to be issued by EDISU. The applicant must take this into account when calculating the time needed to complete and submit the application within the deadlines set in the notice of competition, assuming full responsibility for it.

# ART. 11 SPECIFIC PROVISIONS FOR THE FIRST YEARS OF A MASTER’S DEGREE

Students applying for EDISU 2025/26 benefits for a First Year of a Master’s Degree need not be graduates at the time the application is submitted 

All students who intend to enrol in a Master's degree course during the academic year 2025/26 in accordance with arts. 9 and 11 of this notice of competition must apply within the deadlines as First-Year students: 

a) if they enrol by 30 November 2025, they will be included in the definitive rankings of 16 December 2025 

b) if they do not enrol by 30 November 2025, they must refer to art. 11(2) below. 

International students not residing in Italy must refer to articles 31 (1.1) (for non-EU students) and (2) (for EU students). 

# Art. 11(1) APPLICATION CONVERSION

If students enrolled in a degree course during the academic year 2022/23 apply for the first year of a master’s degree but do not enrol, they may inform EDISU by 12 November 2025 by means of a special complaint procedure, indicating the data for the bachelor's degree course. The application will be converted into an application for subsequent years for the additional semester of a bachelor's degree, if they have not graduated by September 2025 and if they meet the merit requirements. 

Students who apply for a first-level degree career with enrolment prior to 2022/23 but who, following checks with the University indicated in their application, are found to be enrolled in the first year of a Master's degree course, will be included in the rankings for that career. 

If students apply for the subsequent year for the additional semester of a bachelor’s degree but enrol in a master's degree course by 30 November 2025, they may inform EDISU by 12:00 p.m. on 12 November via a special complaint procedure, indicating the details of the master's degree course; the application will be converted into a first-year, master’s degree application, if they meet the requirements. 

# Art. 11(2) FAILURE TO ENROL BY 30 NOVEMBER 2025

If students applying for the first year of the Master's degree are not enrolled in the Master's degree course by 30 November 2025, they will have the outcome “suspended for non-enrolment” in the final Scholarship rankings of 16 December 2025 and will have to enrol by 3 April 2026. 

These students will be included in the provisional rankings of 20 March 2026 and may lodge a complaint by 12:00 p.m. on 3 April 2026. They will then be included in the final Scholarship rankings on 30 April 2026 (12:00 p.m.). 

Successful 2024/25 scholarship-winning students in their final course year will have priority in these rankings. 

If they do not enrol and meet the merit requirements for the additional semester grant, they will have to file a complaint and the application will be converted back to an additional semester application if they have not graduated by September 2025 and meet the merit requirements. 

Students included in the rankings of 30 April 2026 must achieve 20 credits by 10 August 2026 to be eligible for the second 2025/26 grant instalment, including the integration for the second course. 

In order to apply for the scholarship for the 2026/27 academic year, they must achieve the required credits for the scholarship application by 10 August 2026. 

If these students also apply for the accommodation service: 

• if they are allocated a spot but do not enrol for a First Year of a Master’s Degree by 3 April 2026, will not only be excluded from the rankings on 30 April 2026 but will also have to vacate the residence and pay the daily rate of €8.18 for the period of residence. 

• if they are included in the “single sliding list” referred to in art. 33(3) of this notice of competition and enrol in a First Year of a Master's Degree by 3 April 2026, they shall not be removed from the “single sliding list” 

International students not residing in Italy must refer to articles 31 (1.1) (for non-EU students) and (1.2) (for EU students). 

# ART. 12 RANKINGS AND COMPLAINTS

Interested students will make sure to view the rankings in the manner indicated below as no further communications will be sent. The rankings will be published on your personal Online Helpdesk page, “Scholarship” section, by clicking on “Ranking”. Students who have applied for both the accommodation service and the grant must consult two separate rankings: the first for the accommodation service, the second for the scholarship. 

For each benefit applied for, first a provisional ranking and then a definitive ranking will be published. 

After the deadline for the submission of grant applications, before the publication of the provisional grant ranking and in the period between the publication of the provisional and final grant rankings, checks will be carried out with the Universities in order to ascertain the regular enrolment of students and any merit requirements. The provisional and final scholarship rankings will incorporate the results of these assessments. 

The accommodation service rankings will instead be drawn up on the basis of self-certified data from students. 

At the request of students, checks may also be carried out when the application is being completed in particular situations. 

![image](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2026-02-26/96fe0d1f-109c-4be1-a3cb-bd4e5e023921/b3b7903de5239e6809f86cdb8f2c68790d36f454cd059de6679c9555a3cba319.jpg)


No individual communication will be sent regarding the outcome of the competitions. The rankings can only be consulted on your personal Online Helpdesk page (by clicking on “Ranking” in the “Scholarship” section) and at EDISU counters. 

# Art. 12(1) CRITERIA FOR DRAWING UP THE RANKINGS

For students enrolled in the first years of bachelor’s degree, single-cycle master’s degree, and master's degree courses who submit a Standard Application, the grants are allocated on the basis of the provisions of art. 1(4). 

The rankings are divided by University and course level (bachelor’s degree, single-cycle master's degree, and master's degree), without distinction between departments, and within each level they are ordered in ascending order on the basis of the ISEE University (ISEE Parificato for non-EU students with family residing in a non-EU country). If the ISEE Universitario is the same, younger students have priority.51 

The accommodation service rankings are formulated in the same way as for the scholarship, guaranteeing at least one spot per university. 

In drawing up the accommodation service rankings, a standard first-year ranking will be drawn up for each location for students with non-EU citizenship and a household resident in a non-EU country and students with international protection status, as provided for in point 1 of art. 4(1), for which $1 5 \%$ of the spots allocated to each University for first-year students will be reserved. 

# Art. 12(2) PROVISIONAL RANKINGS

Two outcomes are possible in the provisional ranking: 

1. Eligible: students meet the requirements of the notice of competition; they must therefore wait for the publication of the definitive ranking. 

2. Excluded: students do not meet the requirements of the notice of competition or have made material errors when completing the application. If errors can be rectified at the complaint stage, the words “can be rectified by complaint” will be indicated. If students do not rectify their exclusion at the complaint stage against the provisional ranking, they will be disqualified. 

Students who have won or been allocated a place in an EDISU residence and who are excluded from the provisional grant ranking, if: 

1. they do not wish to lodge a complaint, must leave the residence within 3 working days from the date of publication of the provisional grant ranking and pay the daily rate of $\notin 8 . 1 8$ for the period of residence; 

2. they submit a complaint, shall do so in the manner indicated in art. 7(6) and within the time limits indicated in paragraph 5 of this article. 

# Art. 12(3) COMPLAINTS

Students excluded from the provisional rankings, or eligible students who need to change their data, may submit a complaint via the online procedure in accordance with the procedures set out in art. 7(6) and within the deadlines indicated in art. 7(5). The outcomes of the complaints will be available with the publication of the definitive rankings. 

Students who do NOT intend to accept the requested accommodation service must submit their withdrawal by 12:00 p.m. on 22 September 2025, by completing the special complaint against the provisional accommodation service ranking. Otherwise, should they be awarded accommodation and scholarship, they will receive the amount corresponding to the “commuter” type. 

# Art. 12(4) FINAL ACCOMMODATION RANKINGS

Three outcomes are possible: 

1. Winner: students meet the requirements set out in the notice of competition and are entitled to accommodation in EDISU residences; they must also accept the online accommodation service in the manner set out in art. 33(1). 

Eligible: students who meet the requirements set out in the notice of competition but are not eligible for the accommodation service at EDISU residences due to a shortage of available beds, must also declare their interest in the online accommodation service in accordance with the procedures set out in art. 33(2). 

3. Excluded: students do not meet the requirements of the notice of competition or have not rectified material errors present in the application via complaint. 

If students change course location after the publication of the final accommodation service rankings or scrolling rankings, they will be placed at the end of the definitive ranking or scrolling ranking of the new course location. If there is more than one student to be placed in the new course location, the order of placement will be based on the date and time of notification by the student of the change of course location. They must, in any case, be accepted at the location indicated in the final ranking. 

With regard to the rankings for PhDs and Specialisation Schools, please refer to Section VI. 

EDISU will publish definitive rankings according to course type and date of enrolment. 

# Art. 12(5.1) FIRST DEFINITIVE RANKINGS FOR STUDENTS IN FIRST YEAR OF BACHELOR’S OR SINGLE-CYCLE MASTER’S DEGREE WITH ENROLMENT BY 31 OCTOBER 2025

These rankings only include students who meet the requirements and have enrolled for a Bachelor's or single-cycle Master's degree course by 31 October. Two outcomes are possible: 

1. Winner: students meet the requirements of the notice of competition and have the right to take up the scholarship. 

2. Eligible: students who meet the requirements of the notice of competition but cannot take up the scholarship due to a lack of available resources; they must also follow the provisions set out in arts. 5 and 12. 

The eligible candidates in these rankings will be included in the subsequent December rankings, in priority position 

# Art. 12(5.2) GENERAL DEFINITIVE RANKINGS

These rankings include all students applying for scholarships, with the exception of students already successful in previous rankings. Five outcomes are possible: 

1. Winner: students meet the requirements of the notice of competition and have the right to take up the scholarship. 

2. Eligible: students who meet the requirements of the notice of competition but cannot take up the benefit applied for due to a lack of available resources; they must also follow the provisions set out in 5 and 12. 

3. Suspended: students applying or scholarships who have not been duly enrolled by 30 November 2025 will be included in the final December scholarship rankings with the result “suspended”. 

4. Suspended for filter semester enrolment: students requesting the benefit for the first year of medicina e chirurgia, medicina veterinaria e odontoiatria e protesi dentaria courses courses attending the filter semester at a Piedmont university will have the outcome "suspended for filter semester" in December and must follow the instructions of art. 9(3) and 12(5.4) 

5. Excluded: students do not meet the requirements of the notice of competition or have not rectified material errors present in the application via complaint. 

Students who are not included in the rankings of November 7 will be able to submit a new appeal from 12:00 PM on November 7 to 12:00 PM on November 12 

# Art. 12(5.3) DEFINITIVE RANKINGS FOR STUDENTS SUSPENDED IN DECEMBER FOR "ENROLLMENT IN FILTER SEMESTER" AT A PIEDMONT UNIVERSITY AND STUDENTS APPLYING AFTER FILTER SEMESTER

These rankings include students who were “suspended” in the December rankings. four outcomes are possible: 

1. Winner: students meet the requirements of the notice of competition and have the right to take up the scholarship. 

2. Eligible: students who meet the requirements of the notice of competition but cannot take up the benefit applied for due to a lack of available resources; they must also follow the provisions set out in 5 and 12. 

3. Excluded: students do not meet the requirements of the notice of competition or have not rectified material errors present in the application via complaint. 

4. Suspended: students enrolled in a "non-related" course will have a suspended outcome and will be included in the 30 April rankings 

Students assigned a spot in an EDISU residence who are excluded from the final scholarship rankings must vacate the residence within 3 working days of the date of publication of the final scholarship rankings and pay the daily rate of $\in 8 . 1 8$ for the period of residence. 

# Art. 12(5.4) DEFINITIVE RANKINGS FOR STUDENTS SUSPENDED” IN DECEMBER

These rankings include students who were “suspended” in the December rankings. Three outcomes are possible: 

5. Winner: students meet the requirements of the notice of competition and have the right to take up the scholarship. 

6. Eligible: students who meet the requirements of the notice of competition but cannot take up the benefit applied for due to a lack of available resources; they must also follow the provisions set out in 5 and 12. 

7. Excluded: students do not meet the requirements of the notice of competition or have not rectified material errors present in the application via complaint. 

Students assigned a spot in an EDISU residence who are excluded from the final scholarship rankings must vacate the residence within 3 working days of the date of publication of the final scholarship rankings and pay the daily rate of $\in 8 . 1 8$ for the period of residence. 

# Art. 12(6) PUBLICATION DATES FOR RANKINGS AND DEADLINES FOR SUBMITTING COMPLAINTS

Students can check the results by logging in with their SPID or CIE on the “rankings” page of their online helpdesk. International students without residence in Italy, on the other hand, must access results using a Temporary Access Code. 

Students who are interested may complaint against the final results of the ranking to the Regional Administrative Court of Piedmont within 60 days of publication. 

They may also complaint to the Head of State within 120 days of publication. 

# ART. 13 MERIT REQUIREMENTS, SCHOLARSHIP INCREASE FOR ENROLMENT IN SECOND COURSE, DISBURSEMENT PERIOD

Students enrolled in the first years who are successful in the final scholarship rankings receive the scholarship amounts in accordance with paragraph 4 below: “Scholarship disbursement period” 

# Art. 13(1) MERIT REQUIREMENTS FOR SECOND INSTALMENT

To obtain the second grant instalment, students must obtain the credits listed in the table below by 10 August 2026 in accordance with the terms and timing set out in paragraph 4 below. These provisions also apply to students included in the final rankings of 26 March (suspended for filter semester enrolment) and 30 April (suspended December ranking). 

20 credits 

11 credits 

Full-time enrolment in bachelor’s, master’s degree, and single-cycle master's degree course. 

Part-time enrolment in bachelor’s, master’s degree, and single-cycle master's degree course. 

These credits must also be duly registered by your University on or before 10 August 2026. 

The following may NOT be counted in the sum of credits: 

1. credits from unfulfilled academic requirements; 

2. credits of modules in progress that require further work for the final grade; 

3. credits from individual modules that are not recognised; 

4. excess credits; 

5. credits validated by overseas study; 

6. credits from the 24-credit/60-credit course for teacher training. 

Please also note that the bonus can only be used to apply as a subsequent year; therefore, it CANNOT be used for first-year merit achievement. 

The 18 credits obtained for access to the courses referred to in Ministerial Decree 418 of 30 May 2025 are valid for obtaining the 20 credits required for the second instalment of the scholarship. 

EDISU is not involved in teaching, so if you have any doubts about your study plan or the nature of the credits you have earned, please contact the University. 

Prior to the disbursement of the second scholarship instalment, EDISU will verify the registration of the required credits with the Universities and therefore disbursement will only take place if it has verified that the requirement has been met. 

The outcome of the checks will be published on the online helpdesk on the date of disbursement of the instalment in the benefits history section. The outcome may be: 

• compliant; 

• non-compliant. In this case, there will be a subsequent outcome referring to the merit of the first instalment being verified from 30 March 2027. 

For students who have obtained credits during foreign study/exchange projects, the second instalment will only be paid after the credits obtained abroad have been recognised by their home University. 

If students switch courses during the first academic year after having obtained credits, the examinations taken are only considered valid for the purpose of disbursing the second instalment if they are recognised by the new reference academic institution. 

To obtain early payment of the second grant instalment at the end of June 2025, students must achieve merit by 31 May 2026 and self-certify it by 12:00 p.m. on 8 June 2026, in the manner set out in paragraph 3. 

# Art. 13(2) $20 \%$ INCREASE OF GRANT AMOUNT FOR SECOND-COURSE ENROLMENT

Art. 6 of Ministerial Decree 1320/2022 provides that students enrolled at the same time in more than one course are allowed to obtain and keep the scholarship, increased by $2 0 \% ,$ if they meet and maintain the merit requirements, set out in the decree itself, for the entire duration of the courses. The increase is not due if the student loses eligibility for the grant. Nor is it paid if the student loses eligibility for the increase itself. Students enrolling in the filter semester may NOT indicate a related course as their second course and must follow the provisions of art. 9(3) of this notice. 

The request for a $20 \%$ increase must be submitted when completing the scholarship application, in the appropriate “Scholastic Data” section, or can be added via the “Second Bachelor’s Degree Course” data modification request. The request to edit data must be submitted by the deadline for submitting the scholarship application, in accordance with the provisions of art. 7(5) above. 

Students applying for the scholarship as a first-year bachelor’s degree or single-cycle master's degree student may only request the increase for a first year of a bachelor’s degree or single-cycle master's degree, they may NOT request it for a subsequent year or a master's degree. 

The increase, reserved exclusively for students enrolling in both the main course and the second full-time course, will be disbursed together with the second instalment of the scholarship for students enrolled in the first years of the course, subject to any changes introduced by the MIUR Ministerial Decree implementing Law 33/2022. 

To obtain the increase, the student must achieve 20 credits by 10 August 2026 in both the course for which they applied for the scholarship and in the course in which they applied for the increase, if related to a first year of a course. 

If 20 credits are not obtained in the course for which the scholarship was applied for, the right to the $20 \%$ increase also lapses. If the 20 credits are obtained for the course for which the scholarship is requested but not for the course for which the $20 \%$ increase is requested, the student remains a scholarship recipient but loses the right to the increase. 

In the event that the increase is requested for a subsequent year, the merit requirements on 10 August 2025, as referred to in art. 15 below, are not attainable with the use of bonus credits. 

# Art. 13(3) MERIT SELF-CERTIFICATION

In order to receive: 

1. the entire second instalment (equal to $50 \%$ of the total amount) as from the end of June 2026 

2. the increase for enrolment in the second course as a first-year student (equal to $20 \%$ of the total scholarship amount) as of the end of June 2026 

Students must self-certify the required educational merit through the appropriate procedure available on their personal Online Helpdesk page between 1 April and 8 June 2026 at 12:00 p.m. When completing the self-certification, all examinations passed and registered by the University with the relevant details - description, grade (honours should not be declared because it is not counted and is not compulsory to enter your grade), 

date, credits must be entered. The self-certification must be completed and sent online only and is deemed to have been correctly sent if and only if a confirmation (receipt) is sent to the students' e-mail address. The receipt is also available on your personal EDISU Online Helpdesk page, in the “Ricevute” (receipts) section. 

After the closure of the self-certification procedure, EDISU will carry out checks with the University to verify the actual achievement of the credits declared by the students in order to obtain the disbursement of the instalments referred to in points 1 and 2 of this paragraph. 

# Art. 13(4) SCHOLARSHIP DISBURSEMENT PERIOD

Scholarship winners receive the benefit, according to the total amounts indicated in art. 5, as follows52: 

1. A first $50 \%$ of the total amount is paid automatically as per the table* below: 

<table><tr><td></td><td>FIRST YEARS OF BACHELOR&#x27;S AND SINGLE-CYCLE MASTER&#x27;S DEGREES WINNERS IN THE RANKINGS OF 7 NOVEMBER</td><td>NEW IBAN SUBMISSIONS AND ALL FIRST-YEAR STUDENTS WINNERS IN THE RANKINGS OF 16 DECEMBER 2025</td><td>NEW IBAN SUBMISSIONS AND &quot;FILTER SEMESTER&quot; STUDENTS WINNERS IN THE RANKINGS OF 26 MARCH 2026</td><td>ONLY &quot;SUSPENDED&quot; STUDENTS IN THE DECEMBER AND MARCH RANKINGS WINNERS IN THE RANKINGS OF 30 APRIL 2026</td></tr><tr><td>INSERTION OF IBAN</td><td>By 7 November 2025</td><td>By 14 December 2025</td><td>By 13 April 2026</td><td>By 10 May 2026</td></tr><tr><td>DISBURSEMENT</td><td>20% of the total amount: From mid-November 202530% of the total amount: From the end of December 2025</td><td>From the end of December 2025</td><td>From the end of April 2026</td><td>From the end of May 2026</td></tr></table>

Winners may only receive the scholarship by crediting a current account or prepaid card with a SEPA-circuit IBAN in their name or jointly in their name. Postal savings books are excluded. 

*If the students do not communicate an IBAN by the earliest date indicated in the table, it is hereby communicated that the instalment due will be disbursed during the tranche of payments scheduled in the EDISU timetable following the entry of the IBAN. No ad-hoc payments will be made to students who enter their IBAN late. 

International students, who are not allowed to open a current account under current Italian banking regulations, may enter a foreign IBAN, provided it is part of the SEPA circuit. In order to proceed with the payment, the winner must communicate an address in Italy. Until such notice, payment cannot be made. 

With regard to payments to students from certain “high-risk third countries” identified by current European legislation, delays or non-credits may occur. In this case, EDISU shall not be held liable. 

For more information on how to communicate the IBAN, please refer to art. 7(3). 

2. A second instalment, equal to the remaining $50 \%$ of the total amount, is disbursed based on when the merit requirements set out in paragraph 3 above are achieved and, if required, self-certified, as per the table below:

It should be noted that the disbursement of the instalment means the start of the administrative process, which is concluded the following month with the provision of the payment by EDISU to the Credit Institute indicated in the IBAN provided by the students. The availability of the sum in the current account may, therefore, take place in the month following the disbursement, based on the timing of the individual credit institutions. 

If the IBAN is not communicated by 31 December 2027, the instalments will no longer be due. 

Students who do NOT self-certify their merit between 1 April and 8 June 2026 12:00 p.m. will not receive any payment from the end of June 2026. If they achieve at least 20 credits by 10 August 2025, the entire second instalment (equal to 50% of the total amount) is paid out from the end of November 2026, without the need to self-certify your merit. The same provisions apply for the 20% increase of the grant for the second course referred to in paragraph 2 above. 

# Art. 13(5) MERIT REQUIREMENTS TO KEEP THE FIRST INSTALMENT ONLY

Students who do not obtain the credits specified in paragraph 1 of this article by 10 August 2025 lose their entitlement to receive the second grant instalment. They may, however, retain the right to the first scholarship instalment only $5 0 \%$ of the total amount) by achieving at least 20 credits by 30 November 2026. These credits must also be duly registered by your University on or before 30 November 2026. 

The following may NOT be counted in the sum of credits: 

1. credits from unfulfilled academic requirements; 

2. credits of modules in progress that require further work for the final grade; 

3. credits from individual modules that are not recognised; 

4. excess credits; 

5. credits validated by overseas study; 

6. credits from the 24-credit/60-credit course for teacher training. 

Please also note that the bonus can only be used to apply as a subsequent year; therefore, it CANNOT be used for first-year merit achievement. 

If the student changes their course during the first academic year, for the purposes of the retention requirements for the first instalment, they must achieve the required merit as of 30 November 2026 (20 credits if full time and 11 credits if part time) either before or after changing their course: 

• If the student switches courses during the academic year for which they were awarded a scholarship, only the credits validated in the switch in addition to the credits obtained in the new course by 30 November 2026 will be considered valid 

• If the student switches courses at the end of the academic year for which they were awarded a scholarship, only the exams taken before the switch will be considered valid. 

The 18 credits obtained for access to the courses referred to in Ministerial Decree 418 of 30 May 2025 are valid for obtaining the 20 credits required for the second instalment of the scholarship. 

For students who have earned credits during foreign study/exchange projects completed by 30 November 2026, EDISU may consider credits from validation for the purpose of meeting the requirements of the first instalment. 

Failure to meet the merit requirements set out in this paragraph will result in the withdrawal of benefits, thus: 

1. repayment of the first instalment; 

2. the loss of exemption from payment of university fees, in accordance with the Fees Regulations of their University; 

3. if the students have used the accommodation service in EDISU residences, the refund of the value of the accommodation service used in accordance with the provisions set out in paragraph 5 of this article. 

# Art. 13(6) MERIT REQUIREMENTS FOR MAINTAINING ELIGIBILITY

Eligible students who are not successful in the final scholarship ranking may maintain their eligibility, and with it their exemption from paying tuition fees in accordance with their University's Fee Regulations, only if they obtain at least 20 credits (11 if enrolled part-time) by 30 November 2026. These credits must also be duly registered by your University Student Administrative Office on or before 30 November 2026. 

The following may NOT be counted in the sum of credits: 

1. credits from unfulfilled academic requirements; 

2. credits of modules in progress that require further work for the final grade; 

3. credits from individual modules that are not recognised; 

4. excess credits; 

5. credits validated by overseas study; 

6. credits from the 24-credit/60-credit course for teacher training. 

Please also note that the bonus can only be used to apply as a subsequent year; therefore, it CANNOT be used for first-year merit achievement. 

The 18 credits obtained for access to the courses referred to in Ministerial Decree 418 of 30 May 2025 are valid for obtaining the 20 credits required for the second instalment of the scholarship.

Failure to meet the merit requirements set out in this paragraph will result in the withdrawal of benefits, thus: 

1. the loss of exemption from payment of university fees, in accordance with the Fees Regulations of their University; 

2. if the students have used the accommodation service in EDISU residences, the refund of the value of the accommodation service used in accordance with the provisions set out in paragraph 5 of this article. 

# Art. 13(6.1) ELIGIBLE ASSIGNEES OF A SPOT IN AN EDISU RESIDENCE

Students assigned a place can return to residence in September 2026 if they meet the merit requirements set out in paragraph 1 of this Article by 10 August 2026. On their return, students must self-certify their merit directly at the residence on a special form, enclosing a copy of their student record book. 

Students who do not meet the merit requirements set out in paragraph 1 of this article: 

1. may return for the month of September to a residence identified by the administration, which may be different from the one to which they were assigned during the months preceding the summer closure; 

2. must achieve 20 credits by 30 November 2026, otherwise they will be required to repay the amount of $\notin 8 . 1 8$ per day for the entire period used (used being understood as the entire allocation period even in the case of justified short absences, without prejudice to the provisions of art. 33(4.1) for the “Erasmus Option”). 

# Art. 13(7) DEFERRAL OF LAST 30 NOVEMBER 2026 DEADLINE

In some special cases53 the deadline of 30 November 2026 for achieving the minimum merit levels to avoid the withdrawal of benefits (20 credits) is deferred by three months. The cases are as follows: 

1. The death of a member of the household declared in the application. 

2. Hospitalisation of at least 10 days or prolonged illness of the applicant or a member of the household. 

3. Events falling within the causes of natural disasters. 

For the birth of a child, the last deadline of 30 November 2026 is deferred by 5 months in accordance with current legislation on maternity protection and, in particular, compulsory abstention from work. 

Students wishing to apply for this extension must go in person to the EDISU helpdesks by 16 December 2026 and make a request, enclosing documentation proving their circumstances54. 

# Art. 13(8) PROVISIONS FOR SUCCESSFUL ASSIGNEES OF A SPOT IN AN EDISU RESIDENCE

Students assigned a place can return to residence in September 2026 if they meet the merit requirements set out in paragraph 1 of this Article by 10 August 2026. On their return, students must self-certify their merit directly at the residence on a special form, enclosing a copy of their student record book. 

Students who do not meet the merit requirements set out in paragraph 1 of this article: 

1. may return for the month of September to a residence identified by the administration, which may be different from the one to which they were assigned during the months preceding the summer closure; 

must achieve 20 credits by 30 November 2026, otherwise they will be required to repay the amount of € 8.18 per day for the entire period used (used being understood as the entire allocation period even in the case of justified short absences, without prejudice to the provisions of art. 33(4.1) for the “Erasmus Option”). 

# Art. 13(9) CASES OF SUSPENSION OF PAYMENT

Students who find they owe debt that has arisen or is ascertained after the publication of the definitive ranking or who have an instalment plan in place and are in the process of paying their debt to EDISU, have their grant payment suspended until the debt is settled. 

A similar suspension is applied to students in respect of whom proceedings are in progress for financial verification, verification of merit, or forfeiture of benefits, including in relation to previous academic years, and, for students seeking international protection or stateless persons only, verification of their residence permit. 

# Art. 13(10) VERIFICATION OF MERIT AND WITHDRAWAL OF BENEFIT

EDISU subjects all winning students and students eligible for scholarships and those who may be assigned a place to verification of enrolment and merit conditions, in implementation of art. 6 of the Prime Ministerial Decree 9 April 2001 and art. 38 of this notice of competition. 

# Art. 13(11) REFUND OF REGIONAL TAX

Students enrolled as first-years who win or are eligible in the definitive ranking for the scholarship and who meet the merit requirements of the reference Notice of Competition, are entitled to reimbursement of the regional tax for the right to study. This totals € 140.00 and is paid at the time of enrolment with the payment of the first instalment of university fees by the deadlines established by students’ respective Universities. 

Students enrolled as first-years who were “excluded” in the definitive ranking for the scholarship will not be entitled to reimbursement of the regional tax. Payment of this amount is compulsory for the purpose of regular enrolment at the University. 

The reimbursement of the regional tax will only be paid automatically (without any obligation to submit a request for reimbursement) to students who are winners in the final scholarship ranking as first-years, following the achievement of the merit required for the scholarship as indicated in the table below: 

<table><tr><td>Automatic Regional Tax Refund</td><td>Merit requirements</td><td>Merit self-certification</td></tr><tr><td>From August 2026</td><td>Achievement of 20 credits by 31 May 2026</td><td>Between 1 April and 8 June 2026 12:00 p.m..</td></tr><tr><td>From February 2027</td><td>Achievement of 20 credits by 10 August 2026</td><td>Not required</td></tr><tr><td>By May 2027</td><td>Achievement of 20 credits by 30 November 2026</td><td>Not required</td></tr></table>

Students enrolled at the Polytechnic University of Turin as first-years do not have to fill in the application for reimbursement of the regional tax even if they are EDISU scholarship winners. The management of any regional tax refunds is the responsibility of the University itself. For further information, please contact your Administrative Office. 

For any other information on tuition fees, students should contact their university by consulting the Tuition Fees Regulations and contacting the relevant offices (Fees Office, Student Administrative Office). 

# ART. 14 FIRST-YEAR ACCOMMODATION SERVICE ACCEPTANCE

Detailed provisions on the acceptance of the accommodation service can be found in art. 33.

SECTION IV 

# SPECIFIC

# PROVISIONS FOR

# SUBSEQUENT YEARS

# ART. 15 WHO CAN APPLY: ADMISSION AND MERIT REQUIREMENTS

This section is addressed to students enrolling, in the 2025/26 academic year, in a year subsequent to the first year of a bachelor's degree, master's degree or single-cycle master's degree under the new system55. This includes students who apply for an additional semester and who graduate after 30 September 2025 and students who are considered subsequent-year students as a result of an internal transfer, transfer from another University, and recognition of credits following validation of foreign study, individual modules, withdrawal, or forfeiture. 

Students graduating by 30 September 2025 may check the requirements for applying for a degree award as set out in Section V below. 

In the case of part-time enrolment, you may only submit a standard application and may NOT benefit from the Scholarship for the additional semester. 

Students attending the “filter semester” of medicina e chirurgia, medicina veterinaria e odontoiatria e protesi dentaria courses courses (LM-41, LM-46, LM-42), even at a non-Piedmont university, must follow the instructions in articles 9(3), 10 and 12 and 13(4) of this Competitive Notice. 

# Art. 15(1) ADMISSION REQUIREMENTS

There are different requirements to be admitted to the competition depending on whether the application is a Standard Application or a Confirmation of Merit Benefits. The minimum requirements for admission to the competition are those laid down for the submission of the Standard Application pursuant to paragraph 1.1 below, in the event of possession of additional requirements pursuant to paragraph 1.2 below, the application will automatically be recognised as a Confirmation of Merit Benefits by the procedure. 

Submission of the application as a Confirmation of Merit Benefits does not entail the disbursement of a different scholarship amount if the student wins but only priority in the ranking. 

# Art. 15(1.1) STANDARD APPLICATION

The requirements for submitting a Standard Application are as follows. 

1. Regular enrolment in academic year 2025/26 on a full-time or part-time basis. 

2. Possession of the financial (art. 6) and merit (paragraphs 2.2, 3, 4, 5 and 6 of this article) requirements. 

# Art. 15(1.2) CONFIRMATION OF MERIT BENEFITS

The requirements for submitting Confirmation of Merit Benefits are as follows. 

1. Regular enrolment in academic year 2025/26 on a full-time basis. 

2. Possession of the financial (art. 6) and merit (paragraphs 2.1, 4, 5 and 6 of this article) requirements. The number of credits is higher than those required to submit a Standard Application; in addition, bonus credits cannot be used (para. 3 of this article). 

3. Winning the grant in the previous academic year 2025/26. 

a. If students in 2024/25 applied for the grant only, or both the grant and the accommodation service, but the spot was not allocated (except as provided for in point b below) or they did not accept the spot, then in 2025/26 they may apply for: 

i. the grant alone, as Confirmation of Merit Benefits; 

ii. the scholarship and the accommodation, the former as a Confirmation of Merit Benefits and the latter as a Standard Application. 

b. If the students in 2024/25 applied for both the scholarship and the accommodation service, and the accommodation was also allocated with an admission extension application, or were still on the single sliding list as of 31 May 2025 for the academic year 2024/25 and did not submit the declaration of paid accommodation, receiving the scholarship with commuter amount, in 2025/26 they can apply for: 

i. the grant and the accommodation, both as Confirmation of Merit Benefits; 

ii. the scholarship alone, as Confirmation of Merit Benefits. 

Students who fulfil the above-mentioned conditions and in 2024/25 accepted the accommodation service with the Erasmus Monthly, Erasmus Yearly or Renato Einaudi Option may also confirm their spot on merit. Students who in 2024/25 accepted the accommodation service with the Renato Einaudi Option, however, can only confirm their accommodation on merit in 2025/26 by selecting the same option again. Otherwise, such students’ request for accommodation service will be considered as a Standard Application. EDISU will carry out checks with the Einaudi College on the actual status of the winner at the College. 

# Art. 15(1.3) SPECIAL CASES

Students who have are transferring from another University, including from outside Piedmont, may not apply as a first-year but must apply as a subsequent-year student. For more information, please refer to paragraph 4 of this article. 

2. If students have to repeat the same year, the merit requirements, set out in the table in paragraph 2, will in any case be calculated on the basis of the academic year of first absolute enrolment for the same course level. 

3. Students who enrol after waiving their studies and obtain credit validation must check, based on the number of credits recognised, whether they can apply as a subsequent-year student, or whether they will be considered first-year students again. Please note that the scholarship cannot be applied for in respect of course years for which it was already obtained56. 

4. If the students who withdraw from their studies or lose their student status have benefited from a scholarship or scholarship and accommodation service for more than one academic year during their previous course enrolment, by enrolling in a new course, they will be prevented from applying for benefits from EDISU for the same number of years as they benefited from these during their previous enrolment. This is also true if they have withdrawn from a bachelor’s degree or master's degree course and have subsequently enrolled in a single-cycle master's degree course, and vice versa. The only exception is if they return the scholarship, they benefited from by the deadline established for scholarship complaints for the academic year 2025/26. 

5. International student visa applicants who wish to change their course of study must check with their University whether or not they can opt out of their studies without having to apply for a new visa, based on the MUR circular for the academic year 2025/26. In the event of a transfer of course or university, reference is made to paragraph 4 of this article. 

6. If students have regularly frozen or suspended57 their student career in previous academic years, the period of freezing/suspension will not be taken into account if no degree-related action (passing examinations, submitting a career plan, etc.) has been taken during that period. To this end, EDISU will modify the year of enrolment of students in such a way that the freezing/suspension period does not negatively affect the calculation of merit requirements (e.g. if a student enrolled in 2023/24 has frozen/suspended their career in 2024/25, by applying for 2025/26 they will be considered as having enrolled in 2024/25). When submitting their application, students must notify the freezing of their previous career by opening a ticket. 

7. Students who “enrol early” from March 2025 must follow the provisions of art. 9(2) and (5) of this article. 

# Art. 15(2) MERIT REQUIREMENTS

In addition to the financial requirements (art. 6) and the admission conditions, certain merit requirements must be met when submitting an application58. These requirements consist in the achievement by 10 August 2025 of the number of credits indicated in the tables available at the bottom of this notice of competition, determined according to the following parameters: 

1. course level (bachelor’s degree, single-cycle master's degree, or master’s degree); 

2. type of enrolment (full-time or part-time); 

3. academic year enrolment; 

4. type of application (Standard Application or Confirmation of Merit Benefits). 

These credits must also be duly registered by your University on or before 10 August 2025. 

The following may NOT be counted in the sum of credits: 

1. credits from unfulfilled academic requirements; 

2. credits of modules in progress that require further work for the final grade; 

3. credits from individual modules that are not recognised; 

4. excess credits; 

5. credits from the 24-credit/60-credit course for teacher training. 

For students who have obtained credits during foreign study/exchange projects, the second instalment will only be paid after the credits obtained abroad have been recognised by their home University. 

![image](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2026-02-26/96fe0d1f-109c-4be1-a3cb-bd4e5e023921/b38cfba21bc15c9aa928fa749882ba5440a89d697c756350cebfc1b653593a5b.jpg)


Students enrolled part-time cannot confirm merit-based benefits. 

# Art. 15(2.1) MERIT REQUIREMENTS FOR CONFIRMATION OF MERIT-BASED BENEFITS with FULL TIME ENROLMENT

The table containing the credits required for the “confirmation of merit-based benefits” scholarship can be found in Appendix A1. 

# Art. 15(2.2) MERIT REQUIREMENTS FOR STANDARD APPLICATION with FULL-TIME ENROLMENT

Ministerial Decree 1320/2021 stipulated that “In the event that the organisation of the courses provides that the student may achieve a number of credits lower than 60, the merit requirements shall be redefined in proportion to the credits actually achievable. 

When determining the number of credits required for the additional semester, a redefinition is also made taking into account the number of credits awarded with the final examination. 

The tables containing the credits required for the “standard application” for the scholarship have therefore been prepared on the basis of the above-mentioned decree and can be found in Appendix A2. 

Students with disabilities of $6 6 \%$ or more or recognition of a disability pursuant to art. 3(1) or (3) of Law 104/1992 must refer to the credit table in Appendix C. 

Art. 15(2.3) MERIT REQUIREMENTS FOR STANDARD APPLICATION with PART-TIME ENROLMENT 

The table containing the credits required for part-time enrolment in bachelor’s degree, single-cycle master’s degree, and master’s degree courses can be found in Appendix B., pursuant to the Regional Criteria59 

# Art. 15(3) BONUS CREDITS

Students who, by 10 August 2025, fail to reach the minimum credit thresholds set out in Tables A2 and B, which are an integral part of this notice of competition, have the opportunity to benefit from “bonus” credits that are accrued on the basis of the year attended, starting from the year of first enrolment in bachelor’s degree or single-cycle master's degree courses and according to the following progression: 

1. Students enrolled full-time. 

a. 5 bonuses: to claim benefits for the second year; 

b. 12 bonuses: to claim benefits for the third year; 

c. 15 bonuses: to claim benefits for years after the third year. 

2. Students enrolled part-time. 

a. 3 bonuses: to claim benefits for the second year; 

b. 6 bonuses: to claim benefits for the third year. 

c. 9 bonuses: to apply for benefits for years after the third year (single-cycle master’s degree courses) 

Once used, the bonus available to the student may no longer be increased, but any remaining bonus share may be used in subsequent years. 

During enrolment in a master's degree course, NO new “bonus” credits are accrued; therefore, students enrolled in subsequent years of master's degree courses may only benefit from any remaining, unused bonus credits (if enrolled on a part-time basis, they will have a maximum of 9 “bonus” credits available). 

Students who have completed their bachelor's degree abroad automatically have a residual 15 “bonus” credits. 

Only students who have graduated from a non-Piedmontese Italian university must self-certify the number of residual “bonus” credits in the application for benefits (only indicate 0 residual “bonus” credits if you used them in full during your previous degree career). Students who did not apply for any scholarships during their enrolment in the bachelor’s degree have the maximum number of bonus credits accrued available. 

In the event of the declaration of residual bonuses (between 1 and 15) and should it be necessary to use them for the current academic year, EDISU will check with the reference agency for the right to study for one's degree. 

For all students, the bonus will be awarded automatically in the right number for meeting the minimum merit requirement. Any bonus credits used out of the number of available bonuses will be visible in the ranking. 

# Please note:

1. bonus credits can only be used to reach the minimum merit thresholds for admission to the competition (Standard Application); they cannot be used to reach the merit required for Confirmation of Merit Benefits; 

2. students enrolled in master's degree courses who were enrolled in bachelor’s degree courses under the old system are not eligible for bonuses; 

3. bonus credits have value only in the year of use and will not be counted in subsequent years as credits earned. It should be noted, in fact, that “bonuses” are additional credits provided solely to enable students lacking certain credits to be admitted to the competition for the academic year 2025/26; they do not contribute to the calculation of the merit score nor to the calculation of the ranking score (art. 17(2)) 

4. bonus credits may NOT be used to meet the merit requirements for the course for which the possible $20 \%$ increase in the grant amount is being applied for, in the event of enrolment in a subsequent year. 

![image](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2026-02-26/96fe0d1f-109c-4be1-a3cb-bd4e5e023921/a3e9b96c3ce5ae6760b99bb818c5675168ff5feb4824143caeea5f02f09fe89f.jpg)


Please also note that the bonus can only be used to apply as a subsequent-year bonus; it CANNOT therefore be used for firstyear merit (art. 13) 

Students who transfer: 

1. courses within the same University 

2. between Piedmont Universities, or from a non-Piedmont University 

must apply as a subsequent-year student and must fill in the specific entries “Transfer from Another University” or “Internal course transfer” in the Merit section of the online application. 

Changing course within the same University and transferring from another University, even if not in Piedmont, does not amount to a career break. Therefore, following a transfer, the year of first enrolment will be considered to be that of the previous course and an application cannot be submitted as a first-year student, irrespective of the course year in which the student is enrolled by the University or AFAM, as laid down by Ministerial Decree 1320/2021 and the Regional Criteria. 

For example, if students begin their student career in a Bachelor of Science in Nursing course at the University of Turin in the academic year 2023/24 or in the academic year 2025/26 and switch to the Biology Degree course, the year of first enrolment in the latter course will also be considered 2023/24 for the purposes of awarding the scholarship. 

The same provisions also apply in the event of a transfer from a bachelor’s degree course to a single-cycle master’s degree course and vice versa. 

Merit requirements will therefore be calculated on the basis of the year of first enrolment: students must possess the required number of credits by 10 August 2025 and at least as many credits must be validated following the transfer. Credits earned before transfers and not validated cannot be taken into account. 

In order to be included in the final scholarship rankings of 16 December 2025, students must have their credits validated by 30 November 2025. Should the validation be decided after this date, EDISU will verify that the students have maintained the merit requirements. 

Only the total credits provided by the Universities will be considered valid; any discrepancies between the credits declared by students and those confirmed by the University must be clarified by students at their own University. 

If credit recognition takes place: 

1. by the application submission: students are required to declare this by means of the special option available under the “Scholastic data” > “Merit” section of the online application; 

2. after the application has been submitted, but no later than 12 November 2025: students are required to notify EDISU of this by filling in the special data modification or complaint section; 

3. after 12 November 2025: students are required to promptly notify EDISU of this by opening a ticket as an accredited user. 

When submitting their applications, students must declare validation or pending validation, and it is the student's responsibility to inform EDISU as soon as they have obtained it. 

Students who have declared a change of course or transfer by 30 November 2025, for whom the Validation procedure will not have been completed by the University as of 30 November 2025, will be “suspended” in the definitive rankings of 16 December and may be included in the rankings of 30 April 2026 if the required credits are validated by 3 April 2026. The awarding of the scholarship is subject to the availability of funds. 

# Art. 15(5) CREDIT RECOGNITION (CAREER SHORTENING, SINGLE COURSES, PREVIOUS CAREERS)

Students who obtain: 

a. a career shortening60, as a result of the recognition of credits related to degrees obtained or examinations taken at a foreign University; 

b. recognition of credits from individual courses/modules previously taken61; 

c. recognition of credits from a previous career that has been terminated due to withdrawal, forfeiture, or recognition of credits obtained as an “incoming” student visiting a Piedmont University with a foreign study/exchange project; 

d. recognition of credits for a single-cycle degree master’s degree course after graduation must declare it by entering the “Validations” page available under the “Scholastic data” section of the online application. 

In the rankings, the academic year of first enrolment will be backdated for EDISU purposes only according to the number of credits recognised, as described below: 

1. Bachelor’s degrees courses 

a. 0 to 24 credits: no change 

b. 25 to 79 credits: backdated by one year 

c. 80 to 134 credits: backdated by two years 

d. 135 or more credits: backdated by three years 

2. Master’s degree courses 

a. 0 to 29 credits: no change 

b. 30 to 79 credits: backdated by one year 

c. 80 or more credits: backdated by two years 

3. Single-cycle master’s degree courses 

a. 0 to 24 credits no change 

b. 25 to 79 credits: backdated by one year 

c. 80 to 134 credits: backdated by two years 

d. 135 to 189 credits: backdated by three years 

e. 190 to 244 credits: backdated by four years 

f. 245 to 299 credits: backdated by five years 

g. 300 or more credits: backdated by six years 

The above table is conditional on the possibility of achieving the required credits in the student career. Otherwise, reference is made to art. 15(2) above and Annex A2. 

Credits recognised for various reasons (career shortening, single courses, previous careers) are added together for the purpose of assessing the year of enrolment, even if the recognition took place in an academic year prior to 2025/26. 

Only the total credits provided by the Universities will be considered valid; any discrepancies between the credits declared by students and those confirmed by the University must be clarified by students at their own University. 

Credits registered as a result of the supplementary test will be considered fully taken in Italy. 

In the case of enrolment in a single-cycle degree course following the award of a bachelor's degree, students must have a minimum of 135 validated credits to apply for the scholarship and will be placed in a fourth year of a course. 

It should be noted that for students with a disability of $6 6 \%$ or more or recognition of a disability pursuant to art. 3(1) and/or (3) of Law 104/1992, the number of validated credits is reduced pursuant to art. 29(3.2). 

If, at the time of submitting their application, students have already applied to their University for the foreign career shortening, recognition of individual courses/modules, or validation of credits from their previous career ended due to withdrawal or loss of status, they must declare this by means of the special procedure in the “Scholastic data” section of the online application. Otherwise, it remains the student's responsibility to inform EDISU. 

# If credit recognition takes place:

1. by the application submission: students are required to declare this by means of the special option available under the “Scholastic data” > “Merit” section of the online application; 

2. after the application has been submitted, but no later than 12 November 2025: students are required to notify EDISU of this by filling in the special data modification or complaint section; 

3. between 12 and 30 November 2025: students are required to promptly notify EDISU of this by opening a ticket as an accredited user. 

4. after 30 November 2025: students are required to promptly notify EDISU of this by opening a ticket as an accredited user but will not be subject to changes in the academic year 2025/26. In the academic year 2026/27, on the other hand, the academic year of first enrolment of students will be backdated according to the number of credits recognised and therefore the credits for that year will be required. 

Changes may also occur as a result of automatic checks during the academic year. 

The above provisions also apply in the case of “early registration” from March 2025. 

For the purposes of calculating marks, if the university does not award a mark for validated examinations, the average of the examinations taken in Italy will be taken into account. If students have not taken any examinations in Italy, the average lowest Clevel grade of the ECTS average of the course attended, which the University that establishes it each year for each course of study communicates to EDISU, will be taken into account for calculating the merit mark. 

# Art. 15(6) PARTICIPANTS IN FOREIGN STUDY/EXCHANGE PROJECTS ACADEMIC YEAR 2024/25

If students participated in a foreign study/exchange project in the previous academic year 2024/25, for the purpose of calculating merit requirements, EDISU only takes into account credits formally recognised by the University in which they are enrolled. 

If students are still awaiting validation at the time of filling out the application, they must indicate that they are awaiting recognition, using the appropriate entry available on the “Merit” page in the “Scholastic data” section of the application, and declare the departure and return dates (or indicative if still overseas): the procedure will automatically add, on a conventional and temporary basis, 5 credits for every 30 days spent abroad to the self-certification of merit. Any remaining days, but only if more than 15, will correspond to an additional 5 credits. Only the period spent overseas from 1 October 2024 to 30 September 2025 will be taken into account. The weighted average of the examinations recorded in Italy will be taken into account for the 

calculation of the score (art. 17(2)). If students have not taken any examinations in Italy, the average lowest C-level grade of the ECTS average, communicated to EDISU by the University, will be taken into account. 

Following the recognition of credits obtained during the foreign study/exchange period, EDISU will calculate the actual merit requirements and, in compliance with the provisions of this notice of competition, will confirm or revoke any benefits awarded. If the validation is dated after 10 August 2025 but the foreign study/exchange period is between 1 October 2024 and 30 September 2025, the credits will be considered valid for the 2024/25 benefit application. 

2. If students are already in possession of the validation at the time of completing the application and this has taken place by 10 August 2025, they must indicate that they have obtained the recognition, using the appropriate entry available on the “Merit” page under the “Scholastic data” section of the application, and declare the credits recognised when completing the merit selfcertification. 

3.
