If students are already in possession of the validation at the time of completing the application, but with a date after 10 August 2025, they must select the relevant entry and indicate the credits and score of the relevant validation, but they do not have to indicate them in the merit self-certification. Students must calculate their merit points as set out in art. 17(2) below. 

# ART. 16: METHODS AND DEADLINES FOR SUBMITTING AN APPLICATION

# Art. 16(1) METHOD FOR SUBMITTING THE APPLICATION

Applications can be submitted from 25 July 2025. The application submission methods are set out in art. 7(1.1) (for students who have a SPID or CIE) and (1.2) (for international students who have a 2025/26 Temporary Access Code). International students with a household resident abroad must also abide by the application submission methods outlined in arts. 30 and 31. 

Any event occurring after the date on which the application is submitted (award of another scholarship or other financial aid, transfer to another university, withdrawal from studies, change of commitment from part-time to full-time and vice versa, inability to continue studies, withdrawal from enrolment, change of department or course of study, etc.) must be promptly communicated to the EDISU offices and documented. EDISU will check that the requirements are still met and will take any measures necessary to revoke benefits. If this is not the case, EDISU reserves the right to take action in relation to the failure to notify. In the event of transfer to another University outside Piedmont or withdrawal from studies after the publication of the definitive rankings and during the academic year, the benefit won or the eligibility condition will be revoked. 

![image](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2026-02-26/96fe0d1f-109c-4be1-a3cb-bd4e5e023921/5f1ccf8f97a582107774cf2ac8fcef3e4a660cd81d48a7a560ada95cc25e0a13.jpg)


# Art. 16(2) DEADLINE FOR SUBMITTING THE APPLICATION

<table><tr><td>REQUEST TYPE</td><td>DEADLINE</td></tr><tr><td>SCHOLARSHIP AND ACCOMMODATION SERVICE</td><td>9 SEPTEMBER 12:00 P.M.</td></tr><tr><td>SCHOLARSHIP</td><td>9 SEPTEMBER 12:00 P.M.</td></tr></table>

The online application must always be submitted by 12:00 p.m. on the deadline day. This procedure closes automatically at 12:00 p.m. on that day and the countdown is reset. 

After 12:00 p.m. of the deadline, it will not be possible to submit the application even if the failure to submit is due to force majeure or the fault of a third party (e.g. problems with the internet connection or the terminal being used). 

For students who submit their application with a Temporary Access Code, transmission by 12:00 p.m. will only be possible after attaching the signed PDF of the application and a copy of their valid identity document. 

It can take up to 6 hours from the request for the Temporary Access Code for it to be issued by EDISU. The applicant must take this into account when calculating the time needed to complete and submit the application within the deadlines set in the notice of competition, assuming full responsibility for it. 

![image](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2026-02-26/96fe0d1f-109c-4be1-a3cb-bd4e5e023921/e7ea638811ce151d12754f7a0564d9faffb04cedd1808510e3132e42067452ec.jpg)


# Art. 16(3) APPLICATION CONVERSION

If students apply for the subsequent year for the additional semester of a bachelor’s degree but enrol in a master's degree course by 30 November, they may inform EDISU by 12 November via a special complaint procedure, indicating the details of the master's degree course; the application will be converted into a first-year, master’s degree application, if they meet the requirements. 

If students enrolled in a degree course during the academic year 2022/23 apply for the first year of a master’s degree but do not enrol, they may inform EDISU by means of a special complaint procedure by 12 November to be included in the rankings of 16 December or by 3 April if “suspended” in the rankings of 16 December to be included in those of 30 April 2026. They will need to indicate the data for the bachelor's degree course. The application will be converted into an application for subsequent years for the additional semester of a bachelor's degree, if they have not graduated by September 2025 and if they meet the merit requirements. 

Students who apply for a first-level degree career with enrolment prior to 2022/23 but who, following checks with the University indicated in their application, are found to be enrolled in the first year of a Master's degree course, will be included in the rankings for that career. 

# ART. 17 RANKINGS AND COMPLAINTS

Interested students will make sure to view the rankings in the manner indicated below as no further communications will be sent. The rankings will be published on your personal Online Helpdesk page, “Scholarship” section, by clicking on “Ranking”. Students who have applied for both the accommodation service and the grant must consult two separate rankings: the first for the accommodation service, the second for the scholarship. For each benefit applied for, first a provisional ranking and then a definitive ranking will be published. 

After the deadline for the submission of grant applications, before the publication of the provisional grant ranking and in the period between the publication of the provisional and final grant rankings, checks will be carried out with the Universities in order to ascertain the regular enrolment of students and the merit requirements. The provisional and final scholarship rankings will incorporate the results of these assessments. 

The accommodation service rankings will instead be drawn up on the basis of self-certified data from students. At the request of students, checks may also be carried out when the application is being completed in particular situations. Changes will also be automatically made following checks carried out with the Universities on the applicant's merit conditions 

![image](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2026-02-26/96fe0d1f-109c-4be1-a3cb-bd4e5e023921/13f529529024c73ce3afc0feee863f2dcec3ce23401543befacd6fc11fb28f49.jpg)


No individual communication will be sent regarding the outcome of the competitions. The rankings can only be consulted on your personal Online Helpdesk page (by clicking on “Ranking” in the “Scholarship” section) and at EDISU counters. 

# Art. 17(1) CRITERIA FOR DRAWING UP THE RANKINGS

For students enrolled in bachelor’s degree, single-cycle master’s degree, and master's degree courses: 

1. in years subsequent to the first with Confirmation of Merit Benefits (art. 15(1.2)) 

2. in the first year of a master's degree with Confirmation of Merit Benefits (art. 9(1)) 

3. in years subsequent to the first with Standard Application (art. 15(1.1)) 

The grants are distributed according to art. 1(4). 

The rankings are formulated in the following manner and in the following order of priority: 

Confirmations of Merit Benefits years subsequent to the first (also includes additional semesters). The ranking is ordered by decreasing score and broken down by University, without distinction by level and department. If their points are equal, students with the lowest ISEE Universitario (ISEE Parificato for non-EU international students with family residing in a non-EU country) have priority. If the ISEE Universitario is the same, younger students have priority. 

2. Confirmations Merit Benefits first year of master's degree. The ranking is ordered by lower ISEE Universitario (ISEE Parificato for non-EU international students with family residing in a non-EU country) increasing and subdivided by University, without distinction by department. If the ISEE Universitario is the same, younger students have priority. 

3. Standard application years subsequent to the first. The rankings are broken down by University, level and department, then sorted in descending order of points. If their points are equal, students with the lowest ISEE Universitario (ISEE Parificato for non-EU students with family residing in a non-EU country) have priority. If the ISEE Universitario is the same, younger students have priority. 

For students enrolled in degree courses on a part-time basis, the score is calculated by multiplying the actual score by the 1.53 coefficient already applied to identify the minimum merit requirements with respect to those required by the Prime Ministerial Decree of 9 April 2001 in the case of full-time enrolment. 

With regard to PhDs and Specialisation Schools, please refer to Section VI. 

In the event that all students in the above categories are successful, any surplus resources will be allocated to the first-year students. 

The accommodation service rankings are drawn up in the same way as for the scholarship, in order to distribute the beds indicated in the notice of competition among the Universities, maintaining the same percentage in relation to those entitled and guaranteeing at least one bed per University. 

If students change course location after the publication of the final accommodation service rankings or scrolling rankings, they will be placed at the end of the definitive ranking or scrolling ranking of the new course location. If there is more than one student to be placed in the new course location, the order of placement will be based on the date and time of notification by the student of the change of course location. 

The merit score relates to a student's academic career and is obtained by multiplying the credits by the grade for each examination and adding up all the resulting partials. 

The ranking score is the score used to determine the position of students in the ranking and is obtained by dividing the merit score by the number of years of enrolment of the students decreased by one unit (in the case of a second year the merit score remains the same, in the case of a third year it is divided by two, in the case of an additional semester by three, etc.). 

Examinations with a grade not expressed out of thirty (“merit”, “pass”, etc.) are assigned a grade equal to the weighted average calculated on the other examinations with a numerical grade. 

Honours are not taken into account in the calculation of scores. 

a. Example of merit score calculation for 3 examinations: 

<table><tr><td>Grade</td><td></td><td>Credits</td><td></td><td>Partial</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>26</td><td>x</td><td>10</td><td>=</td><td>260</td><td>+</td></tr><tr><td>23</td><td>x</td><td>9</td><td>=</td><td>207</td><td>+</td></tr><tr><td>30</td><td>x</td><td>8</td><td>=</td><td>240</td><td>=</td></tr><tr><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td>707</td><td>Merit Score</td></tr></table>

b. Example of merit score calculation for 4 examinations, including one “merit” without grade: 

<table><tr><td>Grade</td><td></td><td>Credits</td><td></td><td>Partial</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>26</td><td>x</td><td>10</td><td>=</td><td>260</td><td>+</td></tr><tr><td>23</td><td>x</td><td>9</td><td>=</td><td>207</td><td>+</td></tr><tr><td>30</td><td>x</td><td>8</td><td>=</td><td>240</td><td>+</td></tr><tr><td>Merit</td><td>x</td><td>12</td><td>=</td><td>?</td><td>=</td></tr><tr><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td>?</td><td>Merit Score</td></tr></table>

Consider examinations with grade e: 

1. Add up the partial scores obtained to obtain the merit score: $2 6 0 + 2 0 7 + 2 4 0 = 7 0 7$ 

2. Add up the credits: $1 0 + 9 + 8 = 2 7$ 

3. Calculate the average (score $\div$ credits): $7 0 7 \div 2 7 = 2 6 . 7 8$ 

Now consider the “merit” without a grade: 

4. To calculate the partial merit score, the number of credits of the “merit” is multiplied by the average obtained (to be carried out for each “merit”): $7 2 \times 2 6 , 7 8 = 3 7 4 , 7 6$ 

5. Add the result to the merit score obtained in the first step: $7 0 7 + 3 7 4 . 7 6 = 1 , 0 2 7 . 7 6$ 

# Art. 17(3) PROVISIONAL RANKINGS

Two outcomes are possible in the provisional ranking: 

1. Eligible: students meet the requirements of the notice of competition; they must therefore wait for the publication of the definitive ranking. 

2. Excluded: students do not meet the requirements of the notice of competition or have made material errors when completing the application. If errors can be rectified at the complaint stage, the words “can be rectified by complaint” will be indicated. If students do not rectify their exclusion at the complaint stage against the provisional ranking, they will be disqualified. 

Students who have won or been allocated a place in an EDISU residence and who are excluded from the provisional grant ranking, if: 

1. they do not wish to lodge a complaint, must leave the residence within 3 working days from the date of publication of the provisional grant ranking and pay the daily rate of $\notin 8 . 1 8$ for the period of residence; 

2. they submit a complaint, shall do so in the manner indicated in art. 7(6) and within the time limits indicated in paragraph 6 of this article. 

# Art. 17(4) COMPLAINTS

Students excluded from the provisional rankings, or eligible students who need to change their data, may submit a complaint in accordance with the methods set out in art. 7(6) (online procedure) and within the deadlines indicated in art. 7(6). The outcomes of the complaints will be available with the publication of the definitive rankings. 

Students who do not intend to accept the requested accommodation service must submit their withdrawal by 22 September 2025 (12:00 p.m.) by completing the special procedure on the online Helpdesk. Otherwise, should they be awarded accommodation and scholarship, they will receive the amount corresponding to the “Commuter student” type. 

Four outcomes are possible in the provisional ranking. 

1. Winner: students meet the requirements of the notice of competition and have the right to take up the benefits applied for. 

a. Winners of accommodation service must accept it online in the manner indicated in art. 33(1). 

b. Scholarship winners must accept them online in the manner indicated in art. 17(1). 

2. Eligible: students who meet the requirements of the notice of competition but cannot take up the benefit applied for due to a lack of available resources. 

a. Students eligible for the accommodation service must fill in the Expression of Interest online in the manner indicated in art. 33(2). 

b. Students eligible for scholarships must follow the provisions indicated in art(5). 

3. Suspended: students who do not meet the requirements due to the following 2 reasons will be included in the final December scholarship rankings with the result “suspended”: 

a. students who on 30 November 2024 were not duly enrolled for the academic year 2025/26 

b. students who have applied for a validation (for a change of course or transfer from another university or recognition of credits from courses previously taken in Italy and abroad) and for whom the universities are unable to proceed with the validation decision by 30 November 2025. 

These students will compete in the provisional rankings of 20 March 2026 and definitive rankings of 30 April 2026. 

4. Excluded: students do not meet the requirements of the notice of competition or have not rectified material errors present in the application via complaint. 

Winning students or those assigned a spot in an EDISU residence who are excluded from the final scholarship rankings must vacate the residence within 3 working days of the date of publication of the final scholarship rankings and pay the daily rate of $\in 8 . 1 8$ for the period in the residence. 

# Art. 17(6) PUBLICATION DATES FOR RANKINGS AND DEADLINES FOR SUBMITTING COMPLAINTS

<table><tr><td>Benefit type</td><td>PROVISIONAL RANKINGS</td><td>COMPLAINTS</td><td>DEFINITIVE RANKINGS</td></tr><tr><td>ACCOMMODATION SERVICE</td><td>17/09/202512:00 p.m.</td><td>17 to 22 September 202512:00 p.m.</td><td>26/09/202512:00 p.m.</td></tr><tr><td>SCHOLARSHIP</td><td>22/10/202512:00 p.m.</td><td>From 22 October to 12November 202512:00 p.m.</td><td>16 December 2025*12:00 p.m.</td></tr></table>

*Students suspended in the rankings of 16 December 2025 in accordance with paragraph 5 above will be included in the provisional rankings of 20 March 2025 and in the definitive rankings of 30 April 2026 and will be able to lodge complaints from 20 March 2026 to 3 April 2026 at 12:00 p.m. Students with the outcome "suspended for filter semester" in the 16 December rankings who do not achieve the required credits, cannot enrol in a related course but will enrol in a "non-related" course will have the outcome "suspended" in the rankings of 26 March 2026. They will be included in the rankings of 30 April 2026 

Students can check the rankings published after that date by accessing their personal page via their SPID or CIE. International students without residence in Italy, on the other hand, must request a Temporary Access Code. 

Students who are interested may promptly complaint against the final results of the ranking to the Regional Administrative Court of Piedmont and, in any case, within 60 days of publication. 

They may also complaint to the Head of State within 120 days of publication. 

# Art. 17(7) $20 \%$ INCREASE OF SCHOLARSHIP AMOUNT FOR SECOND-COURSE ENROLMENT

Art. 6 of Ministerial Decree 1320/2021 provides that students enrolled at the same time in more than one course are allowed to obtain and keep the scholarship, increased by $2 0 \% ,$ , if they meet and maintain the merit requirements, set out in the decree itself, for the entire duration of the courses. The increase is not due if the student loses eligibility for the grant. Nor is it paid if the student loses eligibility for the increase itself. 

The request for a $20 \%$ increase must be submitted when completing the scholarship application, in the appropriate “Scholastic data” section, or can be added via the “Second Bachelor’s Degree Course” data modification request. The request to edit data must be submitted by the deadline for submitting the scholarship application. 

Students applying for a full scholarship for a full time year subsequent to the first may apply for an increase for a first year full time or a subsequent year full time equal to or lower than the year for which the scholarship is applied for (e.g. a grant applicant for a second year may apply for an increase for a first or second year but not for a third) 

In the event that the increase is requested for a subsequent year, the merit requirements on 10 August 2025, as referred to in art. 14 above, cannot be attained using bonus credits. 

Students enrolling in the “filter semester” of medicina e chirurgia, medicina veterinaria e odontoiatria e protesi dentaria courses courses may NOT indicate a related course as their second course and must follow the provisions of art. 9(3) of this notice. 

# ART. 18 SCHOLARSHIP DISBURSEMENT

# Art. 18(1) DISBURSEMENT PERIOD

Scholarship winners receive the benefit, according to the total amounts indicated in art. 5, in two instalments: 

1. the first instalment (equal to $50 \%$ of the total amount) is disbursed starting from the end of December 2025; 

![image](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2026-02-26/96fe0d1f-109c-4be1-a3cb-bd4e5e023921/5053ccb9b4eb09df19e1645bb0a77c8e284e0c1ca75a8377ae1ba4b64af7d778.jpg)


The first instalment will be disbursed from the end of December 2025 if students provide their SEPA-circuit IBAN by 14 December 2025. 

If students communicate their IBAN by 13 April 2026, the first instalment will be disbursed from the end of April 2026. 

For only those students suspended in the December rankings and successful in the rankings of 30 April 2026, the first instalment will be disbursed from the end of May 2025 if students communicate their IBAN by 10 May 2026. 

Students awarded scholarships with FSE funds must provide the IBAN on which the amount of the scholarship will be credited by EDISU no later than 15 March 2026, without prejudice to derogations previously authorised. 

Subsequent payments of the first instalment are scheduled to coincide with the disbursement period of the second instalments. 

No ad-hoc payments will be made to students who enter their IBAN late. 

2. the second instalment, equal to the remaining $50 \%$ of the total amount, is disbursed from the end of June 2026, by crediting an IBAN from mid-July 2026. per IBAN inseriti entro il 30 giugno 2026 

The second instalment of the scholarship will be paid automatically upon verification that the student career requirements have been met. There is no further merit requirement than required for the submission of the scholarship application and therefore no self-certification of merit must be submitted for the second instalment. 

Possible $20 \%$ increase of amount: $5 0 \%$ on the first instalment and $5 0 \%$ on the second instalment upon verification of the achievement of 20 credits in the case of first-year enrolment. 

In the case of enrolment in the first year for the course for which the increase is requested, in order to receive the second part of the increase together with the second instalment of the scholarship, the student who achieves the 20 credits by 31 May 2026 must also self-certify them by 8 June 2026 as stipulated in art. 13(4). Otherwise, EDISU will carry out automatic checks in November 2025 and, if the outcome is positive, the increase will be paid out in December (preparation of the appropriate deed at the end of November together with the checks for the second instalment of the first-year scholarship). 

Students awarded a scholarship for an additional semester receive a single instalment at the end of December 2025, which will not be revoked if the students do not graduate by 31 March 2026. 

![image](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2026-02-26/96fe0d1f-109c-4be1-a3cb-bd4e5e023921/05d51c639f77002bff3a0b7825b8d21a9945e1af74511ae242eaa97decba5840.jpg)


If the IBAN is not communicated by 31 December 2027, the instalments will no longer be due. 

![image](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2026-02-26/96fe0d1f-109c-4be1-a3cb-bd4e5e023921/8979532ecd9520d22c0e2a6d3878d5af57b8e782287d4d87303aa05a9ea611a7.jpg)


It should be noted that the disbursement of the instalment means the start of the administrative process, which is concluded the following month with the provision of the payment by EDISU to the Credit Institute indicated in the IBAN provided by the students. The sum may, therefore, become available in the current account in the month following the disbursement, based on the timing of the individual credit institutions. 

Winners may only receive the scholarship by crediting a current account or prepaid card with a SEPA-circuit IBAN in their name or jointly in their name. Postal savings books are excluded. For more information on how to communicate the IBAN, please refer to art. 7(3). 

# Art. 18(2) CASES OF SUSPENSION OF PAYMENT

Students who find they owe debt that has arisen or is ascertained after the publication of the definitive ranking or who have an instalment plan in place and are in the process of paying their debt to EDISU, have their grant payment suspended until the debt is settled. 

A similar suspension is applied to students in respect of whom proceedings are in progress for financial verification, verification of merit, or forfeiture of benefits, including in relation to previous academic years, and, for students seeking international protection or stateless persons only, verification of their residence permit. 

# Art. 18(3) REFUND OF REGIONAL TAX

For students in subsequent years who were successful or eligible for a scholarship in the definitive ranking for the academic year. 2024/25 and who, at the time of enrolment, have paid the first instalment of tuition fees, may submit an application for reimbursement of the regional tax of € 140.00 online, in accordance with the Regional Tax Reimbursement Regulations available on the EDISU website. The special procedure must be completed from January to June 2026. 

Reimbursement will only be granted if the benefit is maintained; payment will be made after the second instalment of the scholarship has been paid (Notice of Award of scholarship, accommodation service, and degree award for the relevant academic year). 

Students enrolled in subsequent years who were “excluded” in the definitive ranking for the scholarship will not be entitled to reimbursement of the regional tax. Payment of this amount is compulsory for the purpose of regular enrolment at the University. 

Reimbursement is to be requested via the online application procedure. For more information, interested students are invited to refer to the page Services $>$ Scholarships and other contributions $>$ REGIONAL TAX FOR THE RIGHT TO UNIVERSITY STUDY. 

![image](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2026-02-26/96fe0d1f-109c-4be1-a3cb-bd4e5e023921/a3bf1d3c5464c62c8713006a3929ea99210e3aebb49c75b385286a33f31f0ab4.jpg)


Students enrolled at the Polytechnic University of Turin in subsequent years do not have to fill in the application for reimbursement of the regional tax even if they are EDISU scholarship winners. The management of any regional tax refunds is the responsibility of the University itself. For further information, please contact your Administrative Office. 

For more information on the reimbursement of the regional tax, please refer to the relevant regulation. 

Reimbursement of the regional tax will not be granted to: 

• students subject to scholarship withdrawal 

• students who will be EXCLUDED in the definitive rankings 

• students who renounce their studies after the enrolment deadline 

# ART. 19 ACCEPTANCE

# SUBSEQUENT-YEAR ACCOMMODATION SERVICE

Detailed provisions on the acceptance of the accommodation service can be found in art. 33. 

![image](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2026-02-26/96fe0d1f-109c-4be1-a3cb-bd4e5e023921/d7aa4adcd27b5dd41d97bbb4b8509a051cf533cb9a0e74fa3103a14fd24916df.jpg)


SECTION V 

# DEGREE PRIZE

# ART. 20 ADMISSION REQUIREMENTS AND AMOUNTS

# Art. 20(1) ADMISSION REQUIREMENTS

The degree award is granted to students who: 

have won the scholarship assigned by EDISU Piemonte in the previous academic year 2024/25 

1. in the previous academic year 2024/25 and 

2. obtained their degree in the last regular year of their course of study by the extraordinary session of the academic year 2024/25, i.e. the last session for being considered as having graduated in the academic year 2024/25 by their university. 

The degree award is incompatible with the scholarship for the additional semester. 

If students have already received the grant for the additional semester for the academic year 2024/25 or for the academic year 2025/26, they cannot apply for the degree award. 

# Art. 20(2) AMOUNT

The amount of the degree award is equal to half of the net 2024/25 grant amount minus the value of the accommodation service, even if this has been monetised for students who have received a scholarship with a non-resident amount. The value of the accommodation service that is deducted is € 2,700.00 and net of any scholarship supplement for enrolment in the second course. 

# ART. 21 APPLICATION SUBMISSION: METHODS AND DEADLINE

The application for a degree award must be completed and submitted exclusively online via the special procedure that will be activated on the student's personal Online Helpdesk page: 

1 to 29 April, 12:00 p.m. 

No new ISEE universitario nor consular documents are required 

# ART. 22 RESULTS AND COMPLAINTS

Students must check the result of their application by consulting the results published on their personal Online Helpdesk page, “Degree Award” section, by clicking on “Ranking”. The provisional results will be published first, then the final ones. 

![image](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2026-02-26/96fe0d1f-109c-4be1-a3cb-bd4e5e023921/4c40dfbec38099efbc5c55e4028cd017bee37b85123a1e0423b47755b9597444.jpg)


No individual communication will be sent regarding the outcome of the competitions. The results can only be consulted on your personal Online Helpdesk page (by clicking on “Ranking” in the “Degree award” section) and at EDISU counters. 

# Art. 22(1) PROVISIONAL RESULTS

There are two possible provisional outcomes: 

1. Eligible: students meet the requirements of the notice of competition; they must therefore wait for the publication of the final results. 

2. Excluded: students do not meet the requirements of the notice of competition or have made material errors when completing the application. 

# Art. 22(2) COMPLAINTS

Students with a provisional, “excluded” result may submit a complaint in the manner indicated in art. 7(6) and within the time limits indicated in paragraph 4.4 of this article. 

After the deadline for submitting applications, before the publication of the provisional results, and in the period between the publication of the provisional and final results, checks will begin with the Universities to verify that they meet the requirements set out in paragraph 1 of this article. The provisional and final results will incorporate the result of these assessments. 

# Art. 22(3) FINAL RESULTS

There are two possible final outcomes: 

1. Winner: students meet the requirements of the notice of competition and have the right to receive the degree award. 

2. Excluded: students do not meet the requirements of the notice of competition or have not rectified material errors present in the application via complaint. 

# Art. 22(4) PUBLICATION DATES FOR RESULTS AND DEADLINES FOR SUBMITTING COMPLAINTS

PROVISIONAL RESULTS 

14 May 2026 

COMPLAINTS 

14 May to 26 May 2026 

FINAL RESULTS 

10 June 2026 

# ART. 23 PAYMENT

Disbursement of the degree award will take place from the end of July 2026. 

![image](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2026-02-26/96fe0d1f-109c-4be1-a3cb-bd4e5e023921/790568928280ec921d48bcfc6d157af4c7897f89a0ca698d3d3e19ae59aa94f2.jpg)


It should be noted that disbursement means the act by which EDISU orders payment. The actual availability of the sum in the students' current account or on their card will therefore take place in the following working days, based on the technical timing of the individual credit institutions. 

If the IBAN is not communicated by 31 December 2027, the instalments will no longer be due. 

Winners may only receive the degree award by crediting a current account or prepaid card with an Italian IBAN in their name or jointly in their name. Postal savings books are excluded. For more information on how to communicate the IBAN, please refer to art. 7(3). 

![image](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2026-02-26/96fe0d1f-109c-4be1-a3cb-bd4e5e023921/1aab1960e5928ac90d29499bdd24ec9fcc178547214ea9982864bb1dc0a8d766.jpg)


Disbursements will only be made according to the above time frames if students provide their IBAN by 10 July 2026. 

# Art. 23(1) CASES OF SUSPENSION OF PAYMENT

Students who find they owe debt that has arisen or is ascertained after the publication of the final results or who have an instalment plan in place and are in the process of paying their debt to EDISU, have their degree award payment suspended until the debt is settled. 

A similar suspension is applied to students in respect of whom proceedings are in progress for financial verification, verification of merit, or forfeiture of benefits, including in relation to previous academic years, and, for students seeking international protection or stateless persons only, verification of their residence permit. 

![image](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2026-02-26/96fe0d1f-109c-4be1-a3cb-bd4e5e023921/c94da423a534eeaf5dbb637205199384c60747618e5dfd31d0a3d336b3026a97.jpg)


SECTION VI 

# PHDS AND

# SPECIALISATION

# SCHOOLS

# ART. 24 WHO CAN APPLY: ADMISSION, MERIT, AND FINANCIAL REQUIREMENTS

This section is aimed at students enrolling, in the 2025/26 academic year, in a first year or year subsequent to the first in the courses listed below62: 

1. PhD courses, who do not benefit from a scholarship; 

2. specialisation schools of at least two years' duration, excluding medical schools under Legislative Decree 368/1999. 

The admission and merit requirements for participation in the competition, the deadlines for submitting applications (art. 25), the dates of publication of the rankings (art. 26), the timetable for payment of the grant (art. 27), and provisions for non-resident students (art. 28) are indicated below 

Students enrolled in doctoral and specialisation school courses cannot apply for the accommodation service but only for the scholarship 

# Art. 24(1) ADMISSION REQUIREMENTS

For both the first years and subsequent years, in addition to the financial requirements (art. 6 and Section VII Specific Provisions for international Students - and paragraph 3 below), only admission to or enrolment in a doctoral course or specialisation school is required, which will be verified when the provisional and final scholarship rankings are drawn up. 

# Art. 24(2) MERIT REQUIREMENTS

In addition to the financial (art. 6 and Section VII Specific Provisions for international Students - and paragraph 3 below) and admission requirements (paragraph 1 of this article), for years subsequent to the first there are no further merit requirements for admission to the rankings except for admission to the year for which the scholarship is requested 

The scholarship will be withdrawn if students renounce their PhD during the academic year or apply to free or suspend their student career in the academic year 2025/26. 

If students have regularly frozen or suspended63 their student career in previous academic years, the period of freezing/suspension will not be taken into account if no degree-related action has been taken during that period. To this end, EDISU will amend the year of enrolment of students in such a way that the freezing/suspension period does not adversely affect the calculation of merit requirements. When submitting their application, students must notify the freezing of their previous career by opening a ticket. 

# Art. 24(3) FINANCIAL REQUIREMENTS

Students enrolled in doctoral courses and specialisation schools have the option of requesting ISEE processing according to ordinary rules (with a request for a ISEE Dottorato) or the ISEE Parificato, or of making an explicit request at the CAAF for the issue of ISEE Dottorato nucleo ristretto (art. 6(4)). 

<table><tr><td>STUDENT</td><td>RESIDENT IN ITALY</td><td>RESIDENT ABROAD</td></tr><tr><td>WITH ITALIAN CITIZENSHIP</td><td>ISEE Dottorato/Nucleo Ristretto</td><td>Consular documentation pursuant to art. 6(5) to obtain the calculation of the ISEE Parificato by EDISU Piemonte. Also in the case of married students registered with AIRE.</td></tr><tr><td>WITH EU OR NON-EU CITIZENSHIP</td><td>ISEE Dottorato/Nucleo Ristretto</td><td>Consular documentation pursuant to art. 30(3) to obtain the calculation of the ISEE Parificato by EDISU Piemonte.</td></tr><tr><td>STATELESS or HOLDER OF INTERNATIONAL PROTECTION</td><td colspan="2">ISEE Dottorato/Nucleo Ristretto
The household for ISEE purposes will be identified on the basis of the registered family status to which the applicant belongs.</td></tr></table>

The ISEE Dottorato certificate must be signed and issued as of 1 January 2025. Please note that the ISEE certificate, in order to be considered valid for the competition, must apply, in respect of the applicant benefits, to doctoral courses or, alternatively, be valid for a restricted family, should the applicant wish to take advantage of it. It must also be free of observations regarding omissions/formalities (art. 6(1)). 

Please note that in order to take advantage of the “Nucleo Ristretto” (Restricted Household) option, interested students must sign the DSU for the issue of the ISEE certificate as “declarants”. It should be noted that, in the case of married students, the household for the processing the certificate with the “Nucleo Ristretto” (Restricted Household) option also includes the spouse and children (if any). 

It should be noted that international students may submit the ISEE Dottorato certificate with the “nucleo ristretto” (restricted household) option only if, on the date of submission of the application they have already taken up residence in Italy (art. 6(1)). 

Please note: students enrolled in a doctoral course or specialisation school cannot apply as independent students (art. 6(1.5)) since this case only applies to the ISEE Universitario – not to the ISEE Dottorato. 

It should be noted that the request to process the ISEE Parificato according to the ordinary rules excludes the use of the ISEE Dottorato and the “Nucleo Ristretto” (Restricted Household) option. Please refer to arts. 30 and 31 of this notice of competition for the Consular Documents required to apply for their issue. 

Please note that, if students are resident in Italy while their spouses and/or children, if any, reside abroad, they will need to apply for a certificate for ISEE Dottorato/nucleo ristretto that includes the applicant and then supplement the financial data relating to the members residing abroad by requesting an ISEE Parificato certificate. In this case, in order to complete the application for benefits, both certificates, as well as the consular documentation relating to the members of the household residing abroad (arts. 30 and 31 of this notice of competition), must be submitted. 

If non-EU or EU international students residing in Italy benefit from the ISEE Dottorato or ISEE nucleo ristretto, in the online application procedure they must consider only themselves (and any spouses and minor children) as a family; therefore, the type of scholarship will be subject to their registered residence in Italy (art. 4 of this notice of competition). 

Non-EU and EU international students who need to have their ISEE Parificato calculated must refer to arts. 30 and 31 of this Notice of competition. 

# ART. 25 METHODS AND DEADLINES FOR SUBMITTING AN APPLICATION

# Art. 25(1) METHOD FOR SUBMITTING THE APPLICATION

Applications can be submitted from 28 October 2025. The application submission methods are set out in art. 7(1.1) (for Italian students who have a SPID or CIE) and (1.2) (for international students without residence in Italy). International students with a household resident in a non-EU or EU country must also follow the application submission methods outlined in arts. 30 and 31. 

There are no spots for students enrolled in doctoral courses and specialisation schools. Therefore, non-resident students must only apply for scholarships 

![image](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2026-02-26/96fe0d1f-109c-4be1-a3cb-bd4e5e023921/5322d3be65759342c6e80c03ff6f5e86fe3f70a54df4d7ba26c83b6a1eefbe30.jpg)


Students must submit their applications within the deadlines specified in the following table, even if they were not yet duly enrolled at the time of submitting the application. 

# Art. 25(2) DEADLINES FOR SUBMITTING THE APPLICATION

# DEADLINE

# 28 NOVEMBER 2025 12:00

# p.m..

Students who have already applied for the additional semester of a master’s degree or single-cycle master's degree may still apply for benefits for the first year of a PhD/specialisation school. If they are awarded a scholarship, they may receive one instalment for the master's degree and two instalments for the PhD/specialisation school. To submit an application, this type of student must open a ticket by 28 November 2025, enclosing proof of identity, indicating the University and course and its duration. 

![image](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2026-02-26/96fe0d1f-109c-4be1-a3cb-bd4e5e023921/9ef418d6cf221adfcdecc6d0e7969abfd9c5cd76a30e7245c28b300da9e3442b.jpg)


The online application must always be submitted by 12:00 p.m. on the deadline day. This procedure closes automatically at 12:00 p.m. on that day and the countdown is reset. 

After 12:00 p.m. of the deadline, it will not be possible to submit the application even if the failure to submit is due to force majeure or the fault of a third party (e.g. problems with the internet connection or the terminal being used). 

International students without residency in Italy who submit their application with a Temporary Access Code can only transmit it by 12:00 p.m. after attaching the signed PDF of the application and a copy of their valid identity document. 

After the online submission of the application, the data entered can only be edited online until 12:00 p.m. on the application deadline day, as indicated in paragraph 3 below. The data change procedure remains unchanged with respect to what is regulated in art. 7(5.1). 

For the students referred to in this section, the same procedure for the “ISEE financial data” section may be carried out by submitting a valid certificate for ISEE Dottorato or Nucleo Ristretto for the benefit applicant, free of observations regarding omissions/discrepancies. 

# ART. 26 RANKINGS AND COMPLAINTS

Students must check the result of their application by consulting the rankings published on their personal Online Helpdesk page, “Scholarship” section, by clicking on “Ranking”. 

First a provisional ranking and then a definitive ranking will be published. 

Only after the deadline for submitting applications, before publishing the provisional ranking, and in the period between the publication of the provisional and definitive rankings, will checks be carried out with the Universities in order to ascertain the regular enrolment of students. The provisional ranking will incorporate the results of these assessments. 

Changes will also be automatically made following checks carried out with the Universities on the applicant's merit conditions. 

![image](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2026-02-26/96fe0d1f-109c-4be1-a3cb-bd4e5e023921/7c8b3e81e2a601df9367f638d16e3bfbacf0334adc3c3d65cca0339702966a2e.jpg)


No individual communication will be sent regarding the outcome of the competitions. The rankings can only be consulted on your personal Online Helpdesk page (by clicking on “Ranking” in the “Scholarship” section) and at EDISU counters. 

# Art. 26(1) CRITERIA FOR DRAWING UP THE RANKINGS

According to art. 1(4), those enrolled in the first years of doctoral and specialisation school courses are included in the allocation of $1 5 \%$ of the grants assigned to each University. The allocation is made based on students applying for the grant as first-year students. The rankings are formulated according to the University they attend in an ascending manner based on the students' ISEE Dottorato. Where the ISEE Dottorato is equal, preference is given to younger applicants. 

According to art. 1(4), those enrolled in years subsequent to the first of doctoral and specialisation school courses are included in the allocation of $85 \%$ of the grants assigned to each University. The allocation is made based on students applying for the grant as subsequent-year students. The rankings are formulated according to the University they attend in an ascending manner based on the students' ISEE Dottorato. Where the ISEE Dottorato is equal, preference is given to younger applicants. 

# Art. 26(2) PROVISIONAL RANKINGS

Two outcomes are possible in the provisional ranking: 

Eligible: students meet the requirements of the notice of competition; they must therefore wait for the publication of the definitive ranking. 

2. Excluded: students do not meet the requirements of the notice of competition or have made material errors when completing the application. If errors can be rectified at the complaint stage, the words “can be rectified by complaint” will be indicated. If students do not rectify their exclusion at the provisional ranking complaint stage, they will be disqualified. 

# Art. 26(3) COMPLAINTS

Students who are excluded from the provisional rankings may submit a complaint in the manner indicated in art. 7(6) and within the time limits indicated in paragraph 5 below. 

With regard to the complaint procedure concerning financial data, please note that the ISEE Dottorato with the “nucleo ristretto” (restricted household) option submitted must be valid. 

Please note that, if submitting a new ISEE Dottorato certificate with the “nucleo ristretto” (restricted household) option for year 2026 by means of a complaint, any scholarship amount will also have to be modified with reference to the fiscal year 2024. 

The definitive rankings will take into account the results of the complaints lodged against the provisional rankings and any further checks with the Universities. 

# Art. 26(4) DEFINITIVE RANKINGS

Three outcomes are possible in the provisional ranking: 

1. Winner: students meet the requirements of the notice of competition and have the right to take up the benefits applied for. Scholarship winners must follow the provisions indicated in art. 27. 

Eligible: students who meet the requirements of the notice of competition but cannot take up the benefit applied for due to a lack of available resources. Students eligible for scholarships must follow the provisions indicated in art(5). 

3. Excluded: students do not meet the requirements of the notice of competition or have not rectified material errors present in the application via complaint. 

![image](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2026-02-26/96fe0d1f-109c-4be1-a3cb-bd4e5e023921/8d8ee1a8c57b9810e06f9928874566b372be183818227f7354fbdc4602210fce.jpg)


Any event occurring after the date on which the application is submitted (award of another scholarship or other financial aid, transfer to another university, withdrawal from studies, inability to continue studies, withdrawal from enrolment, etc.) must be promptly communicated to the EDISU offices and documented. EDISU will check that the requirements are still met and will take any measures necessary to revoke benefits. If this is not the case, EDISU reserves the right to take action in relation to the failure to notify. In the event of transfer to another University outside Piedmont or withdrawal from studies after the publication of the definitive rankings and during the academic year, the benefit won or the eligibility condition will be revoked. 


Art. 26(5)



PUBLICATION DATES FOR RANKINGS AND DEADLINES FOR SUBMITTING COMPLAINTS


<table><tr><td>Benefit type</td><td>PROVISIONAL RANKINGS</td><td>COMPLAINTS</td><td>DEFINITIVE RANKINGS</td></tr><tr><td>Scholarship
PhDs and Specialisation
Schools</td><td>20 March 2026
12:00 p.m.</td><td>From 20 March to 3 April
2026 12:00 p.m.</td><td>30 April 2026
12:00 p.m.</td></tr></table>

Since the accommodation service cannot be applied for, only provisional and final scholarship rankings are provided. Non-resident students who submitted their declaration of paid accommodation between 20 March and 10 April 2026 will compete for the nonresident scholarship amount 

# Art. 26(6) SELF-CERTIFICATION OF PAID ACCOMMODATION

Non-resident students are required to self-certify their paid accommodation to receive the appropriate amount due (art. 5(1.3)), only if they are successful in the final grant ranking. Otherwise, if they are awarded a grant, they will be paid the amount provided for commuter students (art. 5(1.2)). 

It should be noted that students enrolled in a PhD course or in a specialisation school cannot apply as independent students (art. 6(1.5)) since this case only applies to the ISEE Universitario – not to the ISEE Dottorato. Therefore, all students wishing to apply for the non-resident amount must self-certify the paid basis of their residence, pursuant to art. 8(2). 

# ART. 27 SCHOLARSHIP DISBURSEMENT

# Art. 27(1) DISBURSEMENT PERIOD

Scholarship winners receive the benefit, according to the total amounts indicated in art. 5, in two instalments: 

1. the first instalment (equal to $50 \%$ of the total amount) is disbursed starting from the end of May $2 0 2 6 ;$ 

2. the second instalment (equal to the remaining $50 \%$ of the total amount) is disbursed starting from the end of June 2026; 

Students receiving a scholarship for an additional semester of a master's degree or single-cycle master's degree and first year of a PhD/specialisation school are granted one instalment for the master's degree and two instalments for the PhD/specialisation school. 

![image](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2026-02-26/96fe0d1f-109c-4be1-a3cb-bd4e5e023921/c284bf03ab7aa244b960f07a4ec39c5b31fcd9663880cdae3f7e0657dd8f0182.jpg)


The first instalment will be disbursed from the end of May 2026 if students provide their SEPA-circuit IBAN by 10 May 2026. Additional payments are planned to coincide with the disbursement period of the second instalments. If the IBAN is not communicated by 31 December 2027, the instalments will no longer be due. 

It should be noted that the disbursement of the instalment means the start of the administrative process, which is concluded the following month with EDISU’s provision of payment to the Credit Institute indicated in the IBAN provided by students. The availability of the sum in the current account may, therefore, take place in the month following the disbursement, based on the timing of the individual credit institutions. 

Winners may only receive the scholarship by crediting a current account or prepaid card with an IBAN in their name or jointly in their name. Postal savings books are excluded. For more information on how to communicate the IBAN, please refer to art. 7(3). 

# Art. 27(2) CASES OF SUSPENSION OF PAYMENT

Students who find they owe debt that has arisen or is ascertained after the publication of the definitive ranking or who have an instalment plan in place and are in the process of paying their debt to EDISU, have their grant payment suspended until the debt is settled. 

A similar suspension is applied to students in respect of whom proceedings are in progress for financial verification, verification of merit, or forfeiture of benefits, including in relation to previous academic years, and, for students seeking international protection or stateless persons only, verification of their residence permit. 

# Art. 27(3) WITHDRAWAL OF BENEFITS

EDISU will withdraw the benefits if it cannot establish the existence of the admission requirements, following checks carried out with the Universities. 

# ART. 28 PROVISIONS FOR NON-RESIDENT STUDENTS

There are no spots for students enrolled in doctoral courses and specialisation schools. Therefore, students who have been awarded scholarships as non-resident students will be paid the non-resident amount if they submit a self-certification of paid accommodation from 20 March to 10 April ${ 2 0 2 6 } ,$ in accordance with the procedures set out in art. 8(2). 

If using a ISEE Dottorato and/or ISEE with “nucleo ristretto” (restricted household) option, it should be noted that the non-resident condition is subject to the registered residence of the students requesting the benefit, as governed by art. 4 of this notice of competition. 

![image](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2026-02-26/96fe0d1f-109c-4be1-a3cb-bd4e5e023921/8e227369883a223facccffb0ba0655cd3cea17fb180cda35a3c7bb689d99d5b3.jpg)


SECTION VII 

# SPECIFIC PROVISIONS FOR DISABLED STUDENTS

# ART. 29 SPECIFIC PROVISIONS FOR DISABLED STUDENTS

In addition to the provisions set out in the previous articles, the following specific provisions apply to students with disabilities. For the purposes of the competition, the following students will be considered disabled: 

1. those with a disability of $6 6 \%$ or more; 

2. those with a disability recognised pursuant to art. 3(1) and/or art. 3(3) of Law 104/199264. 

Recognition of learning difficulties does not constitute eligibility under the specific provisions for disabled students. 

When completing the application form, students must enclose certification attesting to their disability in the appropriate section (indicated in the document “List of certifications to enclose with the application for students with a household composed of one student, holders of international protection, and disabled persons” available in the “Scholarships” $>$ attachments section of the EDISU website). 

Students who, at the time of submitting their application, do not yet have certification attesting to their disability and international students who have not yet obtained recognition from the Italian SSN (National Health Service), must enclose the certification in the complaint procedure by 12 November 2025. Otherwise, they cannot be considered disabled students for the purposes of the benefits referred to in this article 

This certification does not have to be attached if students have submitted it in previous academic years and it is of the “nonrevisable” type. 

# Art. 29(1) BENEFIT DURATION

For students with disabilities, benefits are granted for first-time enrolment according to the following durations: 

<table><tr><td>Enrolled in full-time degree courses</td><td>Nine semesters, starting from the year of first enrolment.</td></tr><tr><td>Enrolled in part-time degree courses</td><td>Eight semesters, starting from the year of first enrolment. These students may apply for the scholarship only, without the accommodation service.</td></tr><tr><td>Enrolled in full-time, single-cycle master&#x27;s degree courses</td><td>Fifteen semesters (for those enrolled in courses with a statutory duration of 6 years) or thirteen (for those enrolled in courses with a statutory duration of 5 years), starting from the year of first enrolment.</td></tr><tr><td>Enrolled in part-time, single-cycle master&#x27;s degree courses</td><td>Fourteen semesters (for those enrolled in courses with a statutory duration of 6 years) or twelve (for those enrolled in courses with a statutory duration of 5 years), starting from the year of first enrolment.</td></tr><tr><td>Enrolled in full-time master&#x27;s degree courses65</td><td>Seven semesters, starting from the year of first enrolment.</td></tr><tr><td>Enrolled in part-time master&#x27;s degree courses</td><td>Six semesters, starting from the year of first enrolment</td></tr><tr><td>Enrolled in a PhD or specialisation school</td><td>Planned number of years for the course of study</td></tr></table>

# Art. 29(2) FINANCIAL REQUIREMENTS

The financial requirements are those set out in art 6. An increase in the equivalence scale of 1.05 is also stipulated. 

# Art. 29(3) MERIT REQUIREMENTS

# Art. 29(3.1) MERIT REQUIREMENTS FOR FIRST-YEAR STUDENTS

For disabled students, the provisions relating to the achievement of merit requirements for the disbursement of the second instalment of the grant (art. 13(1)), and its possible revocation (art. 13(10)), do NOT apply. 

# Art. 29(3.2) MERIT REQUIREMENTS FOR SUBSEQUENT-YEAR STUDENTS

In addition to the financial requirements (art. 6), certain merit requirements must be met when submitting an application. These requirements consist in achieving the number of credits indicated in tables C and $\mathsf { C } \mathsf { 1 } ,$ attached at the bottom of this notice of competition, by 10 August 2025. Such credits are determined according to the following parameters: 

1. course level (bachelor’s degree, single-cycle master's degree, or master’s degree); 

2. type of enrolment (full-time or part-time); 

3. academic year of enrolment of students. 

These credits must also be duly registered by your University on or before 10 August 2025. 

The following may not be counted in the sum of credits: 

1. credits from unfulfilled academic requirements; 

2. credits of modules in progress that require further work for the final grade; 

3. credits from individual modules that are not recognised; 

4. excess credits; 

5. credits from the 24-credit/60-credit course for teacher training. 

The score is determined by multiplying the ranking score, obtained in accordance with art. 2(4) of section 7, by the coefficient of 1.67, in compliance with the $40 \%$ reduction of the minimum credits required by art. 6 of the Prime Ministerial Decree of 9 April 2001, as established by paragraph 2 of art. 14 of the same Decree. 

# Paragraph 3.2 point A Merit requirements with full-time enrolment

Ministerial Decree 1320/2021 stipulated that $^ { \prime \prime } | n$ the event that the organisation of the courses provides that the student may achieve a number of credits lower than 60, the merit requirements shall be redefined in proportion to the credits actually achievable”. 

The tables containing the credits required for disabled students have been prepared by reducing the credits in Table A2, prepared based on the above-mentioned decree, by $40 \%$ and can be found in Annex C. 

# Paragraph 3.2 point B Merit requirements with part-time enrolment

The merit requirements for students enrolled on a part-time basis can be found in Annex C1. 

# Art. 29(3.3) BONUS CREDITS

If they do not achieve the minimum credits required to apply, students enrolled in years subsequent to the first year may use the bonus credits available to them in addition to the credits actually achieved. More information is available in art. 15(3). 

# Art. 29(3.4) CONFIRMATION OF MERIT BENEFITS

Students can confirm their merit benefits for 2025/26: 

1. scholarship winners for the academic year 2024/25; 

2. who renew the application in the manner and within the time limits set out in art. 15. 

# Art. 29(4) SCHOLARSHIP AMOUNT

Pursuant to art. 3(4) of Ministerial Decree 1320/2021, students with disabilities are allocated a scholarship amount increased by $40 \%$ for each type of student. This is to allow for the use of prostheses and supports, as well as all measures that facilitate access to education. 

The amounts, net of € 150 as a contribution for the catering service and including the increase, are as follows 

<table><tr><td></td><td>ISEE ≤ € 13,153.12</td><td>€ 13,153.13&lt; ISEE ≤ € 17,537.50</td><td>€ 17,537.51 &lt; ISEE ≤ € 23,626.00</td><td>€ 23,626.01&lt; ISEE ≤ € 26,306.25</td></tr><tr><td>Resident</td><td>4.438,92</td><td>3.840,36</td><td>3.042,29</td><td>1.845,18</td></tr><tr><td>Commuter</td><td>6.503,89</td><td>5.635,99</td><td>4.478,79</td><td>2.743,00</td></tr><tr><td>Non-resident</td><td>11.236,08</td><td>9.750,94</td><td>7.770,75</td><td>5,380.00</td></tr><tr><td>Non-resident, EDISU residency guest</td><td>8.536,08</td><td>7.050,94</td><td>5.070,75</td><td>2,680.00</td></tr></table>

Students with disabilities who apply for the accommodation service are included in the rankings drawn up in accordance with arts. 11(1) (first years), 16(1) (subsequent years), and 26(1) (PhDs and specialisation schools) without place reservations. 

Students are required to indicate their legal guardian, if any. 

When submitting their application, students may request accommodation for a companion. EDISU will assess the appropriateness of assigning accommodation to the companion based on what the SSN certifies on a case-by-case basis. 

When accepting accommodation, students must declare the type of disability and needs for residence life. 

A total of 60 spots are reserved in the EDISU Residences, differentiated according to the following types of disability for the purposes of safety and emergency management: self-sufficient (50 spots), non-self-sufficient with companion (10 spots). 

The companion of a student with disability who is not self-sufficient must be present in the facility alongside the student and may not be absent even for work. If they do not certify to EDISU that they have appropriate training in emergency evacuation management, they will be duly trained by EDISU. 

No personal services are provided. Students requiring room cleaning or other services must pay the amount directly to the residence hall. 

Applicants will be contacted by the Residence Department for an informational interview after the application deadline. 

Should the student be unable to find a companion, he or she may not be assigned to an EDISU residence and may be eligible for the scholarship amount including the value of the accommodation service if they certify paid residence in accordance with the procedures and within the deadlines laid down in art. 8(2) above. The student will still have to complete the online acceptance procedure (if a winner) or expression of interest (if eligible) and declare their status via a ticket. 

# SECTION VIII SPECIFIC PROVISIONS FOR INTERNATIONAL STUDENTS

# ART. 30 CONSULAR DOCUMENTATION

After filling in the online application (see art. 31), international students must submit the consular documentation explained in the following paragraphs. 

# Art. 30(1) INTERNATIONAL STUDENTS WHO DON’T HAVE TO SUBMIT CONSULAR DOCUMENTATION

The following categories of students are NOT required to submit consular documentation: 

1. International students with their entire household residing in Italy66. 

When submitting their application, they only need to have a ISEE Universitario (art. 6); please note that in this case, non-EU or EU international students must submit their application in the same way as Italian students (art. 7). 

2. Non-EU international students with family fully resident abroad who apply for benefits for a subsequent year of their studies and who in the academic year 2024/25 were found to be beneficiaries or users of EDISU Piemonte benefits/services by submitting new financial documentation or confirming their financial data for the academic year 2023/24 or the academic year 2022/23. This type of student can confirm the financial data of previous years. It should be noted that the confirmation of the financial data presented in the academic year 2022/23 is only granted in the case of enrolment in the additional semester of one's degree programme. In addition, the financial data cannot be confirmed if, in the academic year 2024/25, an application was submitted as an independent student. 

If the family, income, or asset situation of students has changed, it will not be possible to make use of the data confirmation. 

3. Stateless or internationally protected students (see section 5 below for more information). 

# Art. 30(2) INTERNATIONAL STUDENTS WHO HAVE TO SUBMIT CONSULAR DOCUMENTATION

![image](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2026-02-26/96fe0d1f-109c-4be1-a3cb-bd4e5e023921/c63ac91b41a99db415a5f600bace30eb0028f021d4e4765e0318237a2b9b82d0.jpg)


Remember to make a COPY of your consular documentation before sending it to EDISU Piemonte as you will need it for the University of enrolment or registration. In addition, save an electronic copy: this way you will be protected in case of loss and/or theft. 

Students belonging to the following categories must submit the consular documentation indicated in this article in paragraph 3 et seq: 

1. Non-EU international students with their household resident abroad enrolling in a first year 

2. Non-EU international students with their household residing abroad who enrol in a subsequent year and who in the academic year 2024/25 were not beneficiaries or users of EDISU Piemonte benefits/services; 

3. Non-EU international students with a household residing abroad who apply for a subsequent year of a single-cycle master’s degree course and who in 2024/25 confirmed the data submitted in 2022/23; 

4. Non-EU international students who in the academic year 2024/25 applied as an independent student; 

5. EU international students with their household residing abroad. 

The methods for submitting the application and consular documents are set out in art. 31 below. 

# Art. 30(3) CONSULAR DOCUMENTATION

![image](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2026-02-26/96fe0d1f-109c-4be1-a3cb-bd4e5e023921/631aa0e89f10645991034c7d59bfb64fe6a82b2772d17ad268be85bd8a5a86b5.jpg)


Please note: the intervention of agencies or intermediaries for obtaining, legalising, and translating the required documentation is not necessary. Simply request documentation from the authorities in your country that complies with the guidelines listed below. EDISU urges people to be wary of offers to provide help in exchange for money as these can constitute a serious risk of deception. Please note that EDISU carries out thorough checks on all the documentation submitted and, if it proves to be falsified, will proceed with exclusion from benefits (or withdrawal, if these have already been paid) as well as reporting the offence to the competent authorities. 

Students are also invited to read Annex E, which provides more information on the indispensable requirements of financial documentation and special cases and which forms an integral part of the notice of competition. 

The required consular documentation consists of certificates or declarations in originals relating to: 

the composition of the household at the time of students’ applications for benefits, including the first name, surname and date of birth of parents, brothers, sisters and others living in the same household as the students. 

Information on both parents must always be provided. 

In the case of married students, the household consists of the student, spouse, children and any other people living with them. Parents of spouses are to be included in the student’s household only if they still reside with the student or if, although their residence is different, neither the student nor their spouse meet the requirements for independent status set out in section 5 below. 

2. the total gross annual income produced abroad by each individual member of the household aged 18 or over on 1 January 2025, including any siblings and the applicant for benefits. See Annex E for the exchange rate applied. 

In the case of adult household members who have not worked in the reference year, the documentation must show that they are not employed or unemployed for the requested year 

Students with EU citizenship must refer to the 2023 tax year for income earned abroad or documentation of unemployment status while students with non-EU citizenship must refer to the 2024 tax year only. 

3. the existence of movable assets (deposits, current accounts, savings accounts) belonging to each individual household member over 18 years of age on 1 January 2025. 

If a member of the household does not own any movable property, documentation must be submitted to prove this. Only for this type of information can a notarised self-declaration or affidavit be accepted. 

Students with EU citizenship must refer to the date of 31 December 2023 with regard to movable assets held abroad or documentation regarding the lack thereof. 

Students with non-EU citizenship must refer to the date of 31 December 2024 with regard to movable assets held abroad or documentation regarding the lack thereof. 

4. the existence or no of real estate owned abroad for each household member aged 18 and over on 1 January 2025. In the case of real estate (first home and/or other buildings), the certificate must contain the specification of the square metres of the same. 

In the case of no real estate, documentation regarding the lack of property must be produced for each adult member of the household: 

Students with EU citizenship must refer to the date of 31 December 2023 with regard to real estate owned abroad or documentation regarding the lack of such property. 

Students with non-EU citizenship must refer to the date of 31 December 2024 with regard to real estate owned abroad or documentation regarding the lack of such property. 

5. Students wishing to benefit from independent student status, in addition to the documentation listed above, must also submit certification proving that they have earned an income from employment of at least € 9,000.00 (or equivalent in foreign currency) for the 2023 and 2024 tax years and that they have been residing outside their family of origin (in a property that is not owned by a member of their household or other relative) for at least two years from the date of application. When completing the online application, you will be asked to attach documentation proving the residency requirement. 

Students are also invited to read Annex E, which provides more information on the indispensable requirements of financial documentation and special cases and which forms an integral part of the notice of competition. 

The documentation referred to above must be produced and certified by the competent authorities in the student’s own country: declarations, in the form of self-certification or affidavits issued on the basis of original documentation produced and submitted by students, or on the basis of simple declarations made by students or other members of the household, will in no way be accepted, with the exception of certificates proving the absence of movable assets, as in point 3 above. 

Students are also invited to read Annex E, which provides more information on the indispensable requirements of financial documentation and special cases and which forms an integral part of the notice of competition. 

In the event of the loss or theft of consular documentation on arrival in Italy, students must present a copy of the report made to the competent Italian authority, a copy of their passport, visa or residence permit and a copy of the consular documentation transmitted; only in this case will they be able to submit the new documentation during a complaint for the benefit. 

# Art. 30(3.1) Translation and legalisation procedures

The certificates must have: 

a. been issued by the competent authorities of the foreign state where the income and assets were generated; 

b. been translated into Italian by an official translator; 

c. initiated the legalisation procedure at the Italian diplomatic representation in the country of origin (legalisation office at the Embassy or Consulate General) or been postmarked by the competent domestic authority if the State has joined and ratified the Hague Convention concluded on 5 October 1961. 

If students arrive in Italy with only their documents in the original language67, not translated and legalised by the Italian diplomatic authority in their country of origin, they must: 

• endorse and translate documents at their Embassy or Consulate General in Italy 

• legalise documents at a Prefecture68. 

For students from countries where EDISU has identified proven difficulties with issuing certificates or legalisation by the local Italian Embassy only, a certificate issued by the Embassy or Consulate of the country in which the household resides may be produced, bearing the information listed above. This certificate must be legalised at an office of the Italian Prefecture. 

The documents must be translated and legalised by the competent authorities in the year 2025. 

Translations and legalisations dated before 1 January 2025 will not be accepted. 

For those benefits whose expiry date allows it, as of 1 January 2026, the supplementation of consular documentation may take place with translated and legalised certificates in the year 2026. These documents, however, must always refer to the EU (2023) and non-EU (2024) income and assets years, as detailed above. 

The Italian language translation of the consular document must be associated with the relevant original document and indivisible from it. Any separate translations that do not allow correspondence with the original document or its legalisation to be identified will be considered ineligible for evaluation. 

![image](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2026-02-26/96fe0d1f-109c-4be1-a3cb-bd4e5e023921/a66d92e070211f6b6b363b103f924e2082fd77c45b519ca5e9f09a8350627b23.jpg)


Please note that EDISU only takes official translations into account; any errors found in the translations and reported by students via the ticketing system and/or other means cannot be taken into account. A new original copy with new translation and legalisation must be submitted within the deadlines of the benefit applied for. 

# Art. 30(4) STUDENTS FROM PARTICULARLY POOR COUNTRIES

Students coming from particularly poor countries must submit, as an alternative to the documentation indicated in paragraph 3 of this article, a certification from the Italian Representation in the country of origin stating that the students do not belong to a family known to have a high income and social standing69. 

No scholarships or accommodation are reserved for these students, apart from the $1 5 \%$ reservation for non-EU students enrolled in the first years (arts. 11 and 33). 

![image](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2026-02-26/96fe0d1f-109c-4be1-a3cb-bd4e5e023921/e935bd4fd95802c7463c392ee0ba085d505b681d8ba3a61042318136588f4fac.jpg)


The list of particularly poor countries, established by M.U.R. (Ministry of Education, University and Research) Decree No. 440/2024, can be found in table D at the bottom of the notice of competition70. 

# Art. 30(5) STUDENTS HOLDING INTERNATIONAL PROTECTION AND STATELESS PERSONS

Students that have international protection must present, as an alternative to the documentation indicated in section 3 of this article, their residence permit indicating the type of international protection. 

If the residence permit has not yet been issued, the “attestato nominativo” (name and data certificate) that may be issued by the Questura or the order issued by the competent Regional Commission in which the international protection status is recognised may be presented. 

In the event of a refusal to recognise international protection (with the exception of cases where the application is rejected on the grounds that it is manifestly unfounded), students will be asked to produce appropriate documentation attesting to the lodging of a complaint against this decision and, if necessary, a copy of the residence permit of limited duration issued pending the decision of the Court. In this case, the students will then be required, if their complaint is successful, to submit a copy of the residence permit issued to them showing their recognised international protection status, by opening an “ISEE financial requirements” section ticket. 

Stateless students must submit, as an alternative to the documentation indicated in paragraph 3 of this article, a copy of the residence permit attesting to their “stateless status” or, if they do not yet have this, a certified copy of the judgment declaring their statelessness. 

Students under international protection and stateless persons must have a ISEE Universitario as regulated by art. 6(1.1) of this notice of competition71. 

![image](https://cdn-mineru.openxlab.org.cn/result/2026-02-26/96fe0d1f-109c-4be1-a3cb-bd4e5e023921/2f8c8166ceb5777765d316da4d7efb38fc682e53b4264bd4e4fc23d9bf34b917.jpg)


FOR UKRAINIAN STUDENTS ONLY WITH FAMILY ENTIRELY ABROAD AND WITH A TEMPORARY RESIDENCE PERMIT 

Pursuant to and in accordance with art. 274h(395) of Budget Law No. 213/2023, Temporary Residence Permits are extended until 31 December 2025. 

Students from Ukraine holding a temporary residence permit do NOT have to submit the ISEE Universitario or any consular documents relating to their family of origin. They are only required to send the documents relating to the part of the family present in Italy with whom they may reside to EDISU Piemonte according to the methods identified in art. 31(1) of this Notice of competition. These documents include: the identity document and copy of the residence permit of all the family members and any current account balance, including average balance as of 31 December 2023, for the processing of the ISEE Parificato by the EDISU Piemonte CAAF operators. 

Any status other than the one mentioned above will be taken into account when assessing the documentation. 

No scholarships or accommodation are reserved for these students, apart from the $1 5 \%$ reservation for non-EU students enrolled in the first years (arts. 11 and 33). 

Internationally protected and stateless students with their registered residence in the same municipality as the course or in municipalities other than the one in which the course is based, which can be reached by public transport in less than 60 minutes, in accordance with art. 4, are in any case considered non-resident. Therefore, they can apply for the accommodation service and, by self-certifying their paid accommodation (art. 8), they can compete for the scholarship amounts referred to in art. 5(1.3). This provision does not apply to internationally protected and stateless students who have the same residency as members of their family of origin (family reunification) if this residency is in the same municipality as the course or in municipalities other than that where the course is located that may be reached by public transport in less than 60 minutes 

Regardless of the residence of the family of origin, the application for benefits is subject to the students’ citizenship: 

• if the students' citizenship is non-EU or EU, they must comply with the provisions of art. 31 on how to submit and complete the application; 

• If the students have Italian citizenship, they must comply with the provisions of art.6(5) and art. 7 on how to submit and complete the application. These directives also apply to students with dual citizenship who use their Italian citizenship. 

In the case of a household residing partly in Italy and partly abroad, students must have an ordinary ISEE, which must be submitted together with the consular documentation in accordance with the procedures and within the deadline for requesting the benefit. 

Please note that confirmation of financial data is NOT allowed under any circumstances for the part of the household residing in Italy. Therefore, students enrolled in a subsequent year who can confirm their financial data and whose household is partly resident in Italy and partly abroad, must submit an ordinary ISEE 2025 certificate relating to the income and assets of household members resident in Italy, which will be supplemented with the financial and asset documents already in EDISU Piemonte's archives. 

In the case of multiple citizenships, the benefit application methods are identified on the basis of the citizenship chosen at the time of enrolment at the Piedmont University. Students must therefore apply for EDISU benefits using the same citizenship registered with their Piedmont University. 

If the part of the household residing in Italy has a member who generates income and/or possesses assets, in the online procedure, non-EU or EU international students must indicate “family in Italy”. The type of scholarship will be awarded according to the registered residence that the students assumed with the part of their family in Italy. Please consult art. 4 of this notice of competition for more information on the type of scholarship that may be awarded to international students with part of their family in Italy. 

# Art. 30(7) INTERNATIONAL EU STUDENTS

International EU students must submit the online application by enclosing translated and legalised documentation in accordance with current legislation72 regarding the composition of the household, income received in the 2023 tax year, and real estate and movable assets, including average assets, as at 31 December 2023. 

The correctness of the documentation attached to the application for benefits will be assessed by EDISU Piemonte and, through their personal Online Helpdesk page, students will be able to view the outcome after the publication of the provisional rankings.
